出自tedxboston這個開放的演講中 , 理查德・雷斯尼克告訴我們基因測序是如何廉價並快速得顛覆醫療體制 。	in the opening speech by tedxboston , richard resnick told us how gene sequencing cheaply and quickly subverts health care systems .
dna , biotech , healthcare , science , technology	dna , biotech , health care , evidence of nice wisdom .
理查德・雷斯尼克:歡迎進入基因革命時代	rl: welcome to the genomic revolution .
女士們先生們 , 我向您展示人類基因組	ladies and gentlemen , i show you the human genome .
左上是一號染色體	upper left is a chromosome number one .
右下是性染色體	the sex chromosome in the lower right .

在匯入新方向的時候我們要猜測在這個方向上粒子帶有什麼樣的載荷然後我們就能讓它和其他粒子一起旋轉	in the new direction , we have to guess what charges the particles have in this direction , and then we can rotate that with other particles .
如果猜對的話我們就可以在六維載荷空間中構造標準載荷集作為更完美的七維載荷空間圖案的非對稱子集	if we guessed it right , we could construct the standard charges in six charge dimensions and make the perfect symmetry of the sevendimensional charge
這種粒子選擇方法由帕蒂和薩拉姆在1973年提出它是大統一理論的一種探索	this method of particle choice was proposed by patie and salam in 1973 as a kind of exploration of the unified theory .
在我們看到這個新的合成圖案時發現有些空間應該有粒子卻空出來了	when we look at this new unified pattern , we see that there are spaces that ought to be particles that are empty .
這是統一理論的研究方式	this is the way the theory of unification works .
物理學家將已有的結構作為子集探索更大更對稱的結構	physicists explore larger , more symmetrical structures .
這個更大的結構可以讓我們預測那些實際存在卻沒有被觀察到的粒子	this larger configuration allows us to predict the existence of particles that are not yet observed .
這個統一模型推測出了這兩種新子對應的粒子它們應該和弱力很相似但是效果更弱	this unification model indicates that these two new particles should be similar to the weak force , but it's weaker .
現在可以在七維空間中旋轉這個載荷集同時考慮一下關於粒子的奇怪現象:在六維載荷空間中物質的第二代和第三代擁有和第一代物質相同的載荷	now you can rotate this episode of charges in seven dimensions and consider the strange phenomenon of the particles: the second and third generation of matter in sixdimensional charge space .
這些粒子透過對應的六個載荷無法一一識別	these particles can't recognize particles in their corresponding charge .
在標準載荷空間上他們會彼此疊加	in the standard charge space , they superimposed each other .
然而在八維載荷空間中我們可以賦予每一個粒子唯一的新載荷	but in eightdimensional charge space , we can give every single particle the only new charge that we have .
然後在八維空間中旋轉看看整體的圖案是什麼樣的	and spin in eight dimensions , and see what the holistic pattern looks like .
這裡我們可以看到物質的第二代和第三代透過一種叫 " 三重性 " 對稱和第一代相關聯	here we see the second and third generations of matter , symmetries associated with the first generation through a symmetry called " triality . "
在八維中的這個特殊的載荷圖案是數學中最為漂亮的幾何結構之一	this particular pattern of charges in the eight dimensions is one of the most beautiful geometric structures of mathematics .
這是最大的例外型李群e8的圖案	this is the largest exceptional lie group e8 .
李群是光滑曲線形的248維空間	this lie group is a smooth , curved shape with 248 dimensions .
圖案的每一點都能這個極其複雜而又美麗的圖案中找到對稱點	each point in this pattern can find a symmetry in this extremely complex and beautiful pattern .
e8中的一小部分可以用來描述愛因斯坦廣義相對論中用來解釋重力的扭曲時空	a small part of this e8 is used to describe einstein's general theory of relativity to explain the distortion of gravity .
這個幾何形狀和量子力學一起能夠以最小的尺度描述萬物之理	this geometry , along with quantum mechanics , is able to describe something at the smallest scale .
而在八維載荷空間中的這個圖案顯得異常美麗它還囊括了上千種這些基本粒子之間可能的相互作用每一種作用只是這個複雜形狀的一個平面	and this pattern in the eightdimensional charge space is extraordinarily beautiful , and it includes thousands of possible interactions between these elementary particles , each of which is just one plane of this complicated shape .
轉動它時可以看到包含其中的很多錯綜複雜的圖案	as you spin it , you can see many of the intricate patterns containing this intricacies .
透過某種旋轉我們可以在八維空間沿一個對稱軸方向觀察這個圖案並且一次看盡所有粒子	and with a spin , we can look at this pattern in eight dimensions along an axis of symmetry and see all the particles at once .
這是個很美的結構和其他統一理論一樣我們可以看到在這個圖案中有一些空格需要新的粒子來填補	it's a very beautiful structure , and unified theory , and we can see that in this pattern , some spaces involve new particles to fill .
在這有20個空格需要新粒子來填補其中兩個已有帕蒂和薩拉姆粒子填補	here , 20 gaps need new particles to fill in , two of which have already been filled in patisa and sarah particles .
從圖案的位置我們知道這些新粒子和希格斯粒子一樣存在於標量場中但是它們擁有色荷且和強力相互作用	from the position of the pattern , we know that these new particles , like the higgs particles , exist in the quantum spectrum , but they have color charges , and they interact with force .
填入這些新粒子使圖案完整讓我們得到完整的e8	filling new particles into these new particles intact patterns gives us the whole e8 .
這個e8圖案有著深厚的數學根基	this e8 pattern contains deep mathematical roots .
在數學界中它被很多人認為是最美麗的結構	it's thought of as the most beautiful structure in mathematics .
有人預言這個擁有無比數學美的結構能夠以我們可以想象到的最小尺寸描述粒子相互作用的真相	it's predicted that this structure of mathematical beauty can be described in the tiniest possible scale of particle interactions that we can imagine .
而這個數學描述自然的理論並不是剛剛出來的	and this mathematical description of nature is not just coming out .
1623年伽利略寫道: " 大自然這本一直展示在我們面前的書是用數學的語言寫的	in 1623 , galileo wrote , " nature has been shown to us that the book in front of us is written in mathematical language .
它由三角形圓形和其他幾何形狀組成沒有了這些東西在人力所及的範圍裡我們根本不能瞭解沒有了這些我們會迷失在黑暗的迷宮中 "	it's made of triangles and circles and other geometric shapes without these things in the human energy range , and we don't know those at all ; we're going to get lost in the dark labyrinths . "
我相信這是真的我曾試過按照伽利略的指導只用三角形圓形和其他的幾何形狀去描述量子物理的數學性	i believe this is true , and i've tried to describe the mathematics of quantum physics in galileo , using only triangles , circles and other geometric shapes .
當我和其他物理學家在研究這些東西時數學就像一個黑暗的迷宮	while other physicists and i study these things , mathematics is like a dark labyrinth .
但是我們確信數學的核心是純粹美麗的幾何學	but we do know that at the heart of mathematics is purely beautiful geometry .
數學和量子力學一起把我們的宇宙描述為一個在成長的e8珊瑚同時粒子在每個可能的位置相互作用展現出美麗的圖案	together with mathematics and quantum mechanics , we describe our universe as a growing e8 coral , and particles interact in each position , showing beautiful patterns .
藉助大型強子對撞機之類的新型機器圖案得到進一步豐富我們可能看到到底e8圖案還是另一種圖案反映了自然的本質	and with the help of the new machines like the large hadron collider , we're seeing e8 patterns , and another pattern reflecting the nature of nature .
這個探索過程是一個奇妙的探險	this process of discovery is a wonderful adventure .
如果對撞機發現了符合e8圖案的粒子那可太酷了	if the lhc finds particles that fit this e8 pattern , that's really cool .
如果對撞機發現了新粒子但不符合這個圖案那會非常有趣雖然對e8理論不利	if the lhc finds new particles , but it doesn't fit this pattern , it would be really interesting , although bad for the e8 theory .
而且在一定程度上對我不利	and in some ways , it was bad for me .
那到底有多不利呢 ?	so how bad would that be ?
恩那是十分的不利啊	well , that's bad .
但推測大自然的運作總是很冒險的	but predicting how nature works is risky .
這個理論和其他這型別的理論都是在下大注	this theory and others of it are very , very sustainable .
即使花很多精力取得很多成果也不一定能得出自然的真理	and even with a lot of energy , achieving a lot doesn't necessarily have to come up with a natural truth .
理論物理就是這樣失敗是很常見的	that's how theoretical physics works .
這樣看來新物理理論就像新開的公司	so new theories of physics look like startups .
巨大投資後對那些失敗的嘗試情感上總會難以割捨	and when it comes to big investments , it's always hard to get tradeoffs about those failures .
但在科學界如果沒有用就要丟掉它再試試別的	but in science , if it doesn't work , throw it away and try something else .
而在這些不確定中唯一能夠保持理智並獲得幸福的方法是在生活中保持平衡和明察事理	and the only way to maintain sanity and achieve happiness in these uncertain ways is to keep balance and perspective in life .
我已經儘可能保持生活的平衡了	i've been trying to keep my life balanced .
我試著在物理愛情和衝浪中尋找平衡就是我三個載荷的方向	i'm trying to balance myself into physics , love and surfing , which is my three charge directions .
這樣就算我的物理研究沒有任何成果我依然擁有美好的生活	that way , even if there was nothing in my physics , i would still have a good life .
我試著在風景優美的地方居住	i was trying to live in beautiful places .
過去十年我大部分時間都住在毛伊島一個超級漂亮的地方	i've spent most of the last 10 years living on the island of maui , a very beautiful place .

加勒特:不 , 它將會是這個e8型狀對稱性的一部分 。	gc: no , it's going to be an e8shaped symmetry .

黑猩猩沒有語言 , 我們以前提到過	chimpanzees don't have language . we've talked about it before .
但他們確實有一整套非常豐富的姿態和動作其中許多與我們的很像 , 甚至一模一樣並且具有相同涵義黑猩猩打招呼時會擁抱	but they do have a very rich set of gestures and actions , many of which are very similar to us , even identical , and have the same implications for chimpanzees to hug .
他們也親吻、牽手、一個拍另一個的背	they kiss , hold hands , take another kiss .
他們也虛張聲勢地恐嚇 , 或者仍石頭	they're also frightened out loud and rocky .
在黑猩猩的社會里 , 我們發現很多很多憐憫、示愛以及真正利他的例子	in chimpanzees' societies , we find a lot of compassion , love and true exemplification .
和我們一樣 , 不幸的是 , 他們也有天性中陰暗的一面	unfortunately , they also have the dark side of their nature .
他們可以極度兇殘 , 甚至像一種原始戰爭	they can be radically brutal , even like a raw war .
多數情況下 , 這些極具攻擊性的行為是直接針對相鄰社群中個體的	and in many cases , these extremely aggressive behaviors are directly targeted to individuals within their neighboring communities .
這些攻擊大多是為了爭奪地盤	most of these attacks are for territory .
我覺得 , 與別的生物相比黑猩猩更有助於我們認識到 , 人類和動物王國裡的其他成員終歸併無明顯界限	i think it helps us to recognize that there is no final boundary between humans and the rest of the animal kingdom , compared with chimpanzees .
這種界限非常模糊 , 並且隨著我們更多的觀察會一直更加模糊下去	it's a very fuzzy boundary , and as we get more observation , it's going to keep blurring .
我1960年開始的研究一直持續到現在	the research that i started in 1960 is still going on .
這些黑猩猩在野生環境過著複雜的社會生活最重要的是 , 他們幫助我們認識到 , 我們與形形色色的動物在地球上共處 , 我們是其中一部分不能與這些動物分割開來	these chimpanzees live in complex societies in the wild , and most importantly , they help us recognize that we share a lot of these animals with shapes , we're part of the planet where we can't separate from them .
所以 , 發現黑猩猩和世界上其他眾多生物一樣失去聚居地 , 是很讓人難過的	so it's sad to find that chimpanzees and so many other organisms around the world are just as influential as they are , too .
這只是一張從空中拍的照片你可以看到森林覆蓋的gombe高地	this is just a photograph from the air , and you can see the forest covered in gombe height .
16年前 , 我走遍整個地區意識到在公園之外 , 這片森林在1960年時沿著tanganyika湖東岸綿延不絕小巧的、面積只有30平方英里的gombe國家公園就坐落在這裡那時一個問題進入我腦海	16 years ago , i traveled all over the region , and i realized that outside the park , this forest went all the way up the east coast of lake tanganyika in the 1960s , and it was just 30 square miles of gombe national park , and it was sitting down here and there was a question that came to my mind .
" 我們怎麼能進而去試圖拯救這些出了名的黑猩猩 , 而住在國家公園周圍的人卻在為生存而掙扎 ? "	" how can we go in trying to save these famous chimpanzees , and the people who live in the national park are struggling with survival ? "
那裡人口眾多 , 非單薄的土地所能承受	there's a lot of people there , not just a thin amount of land that can bear .
隨著來自蒲隆地的難民湧入來自剛果的人跨湖過來 , 住在那裡的人數增加著	as refugees poured from burundi , from congolese across lakes , the number of people lived there has increased .
那些人非常窮無力從別的地方買吃的	those people were so poor that they bought it elsewhere .
一個計劃由此產生 , 我們稱之為 " 關愛 "	and this is what we call love .
它用整體化的方式來改善住在湖周圍村子裡的人的生活	it's using holistic approach to improve the lives of the people living in the villages around the lake .
剛開始是小規模的 , 有12個村子 。 現在是24個	it starts small , it has 12 villages . it's now 24 .
這裡沒有時間去深入介紹 , 不過該計劃包括象林木苗圃等事情 , 以及適於在山上這片目前嚴重剝蝕幾近沙漠的土地上耕種的方法	there's no time to go further into this , but it's a program , including things like forest beds and things that are appropriate to mountains of land near desert .
控制、防止土地侵蝕的方法	it's a way of controlling and preventing erosion .
收回過度使用的農田的方法以便兩年內這些農田可以重新有收成	and in the course of recycling an overused farm , in just two years , these farms can be reclaimed .
幫助村民從井裡取得淡水	help the villagers get fresh water from wells .
或許建一些校舍	maybe some schoolrooms .
我認為最重要的是與小規模群體婦女合作給她們提供微型信用貸款的機會	i think most importantly , working with smallscale groups of women , giving them miniaturized credit for opportunity .
全世界的情況一樣 , 在所有貸款中我們收回了大約95%	in the same way , in all loans around the world , we've received about 95 percent of all the loans .
使婦女能夠受教育後工作給女孩子提供獎學金 , 以便讓她們完成中學學業很清楚 , 世界各地婦女的教育程度提高了 , 家庭人口數目就會下降	that allows women to be educated and work after scholarship to offer girls scholarships so that they can graduate in the middle schools , and it's very clear that the educational reach of women around the world is going to go down .
我們提供計劃生育和艾滋病及其病毒方面的資訊	we're providing programs for fertility and hiv and its virus .
這項計劃實施之後自然保護方面發生了一些事情	and after implementing this program , something happened in the nature conservation sector .
自然保護方面發生的事情是 , 住在這24個村子裡的農民並沒有把我們看成是跑來研究整個一夥兒猴子的一夥兒白人順便說一下 , 現在很多工作人員是坦尚尼亞人而當我們開始 " 關愛 " 計劃時進入村子的是一個坦尚尼亞小組	what's happening in the nature conservation is that the farmers living in these 24 villages , they're not looking at us as part of a whole bunch of white monkeys , by the way , who are now tanzanians , and when we begin to look at the village engagement program , what we're doing is looking at the tanzanian team .
和村民交談的是一個坦尚尼亞小組詢問村民對什麼感興趣	talking to the villagers was a tanzanian team asking the villagers what they were interested in .
他們對自然保護感興趣嗎 ? 一點也不	are they interested in the nature conservation ? not at all .
他們對健康感興趣 , 他們對教育感興趣	they're interested in health , they're interested in education .
隨著時間推移 , 隨著他們境況開始改善他們開始不斷理解更多有關自然保護的必要性	as time went on , as their circumstances began to improve , they began to understand more and more the need for conservation .
他們開始理解當山上較高位置的數被砍光以後可怕的土地侵蝕和泥流就來了	they began to understand that when the higher positions on the mountain were cut down , a horrible land erosion and mud flow came .
現在 , 我們正在開發所說的大gombe生態系統	now we're developing what we call the gmbe ecosystem .
這是一片國家公園以外的地區綿延包括了所有這些各種各樣剝蝕了的土地	this is an area outside the national park that includes all these different lands that are stripping away .
由於這些村子生活標準高一些他們實際上同意把他們土地的10-20%放到高地一側以便當樹長回來時黑猩猩會再次擁有綠色走廊它們可以藉此穿行以便這是他們基因繁殖所必需的與國家公園外其它殘餘群體互動	and because of the standards of living in these villages , they actually agreed to put 10 to 20 percent of their land on one side of the highlands so that when the chimpanzees came back , they would have green corridors again so that they could wear whatever the gene needed to interact with the rest of the park outside the park .
所以 " 關愛 " 計劃成功了	so , " caring for love has succeeded .
我們在非洲其它地區複製這項計劃在其它面臨極端人口壓力的荒野之地	we copied this program in other parts of africa , in other parts of africa , in the wilderness of extreme population pressure .
但是 , 就像我們在ted開始的所有這幾天一直討論的非洲的問題是主要問題	but , like all of the problems that we've been discussing here at ted over the past couple of days , africa is a major problem .
那裡非常貧窮	it's very poverty .
有大量的人生活在不那麼肥沃的土地上尤其當你把樹砍倒使得土壤裸露 , 任風侵蝕同時處於絕望的人砍倒越來越多的樹以便為他們自己和家人努力培育糧食這樣會發生什麼 ? 有些東西會開始犧牲讓步	a large number of people live in unsuccessful lands , especially when you cut trees out soil bare , erosion the people in despair are killing more and more trees for themselves and their families so that they can feed themselves and their families , and what happens is that some things start to sacrifice .
還有別的問題不僅在非洲而且是其它所有發展中世界 , 甚至是地球上所有地方我們在對我們的地球做什麼呢 ?	there are other questions not only in africa , but in other developing worlds , and even everywhere on earth what do we do to our planet ?
著名科學家 , e.o.威爾遜說過 , 如果地球上每個人的生活標準都達到歐美平均水平我們就再需要三個地球	e . o . wilson , the celebrity scientist , said that if everybody's standards of life on earth reach europe on average , we would need three more planets .
今天他們說是四個 。 可我們沒那些個 , 我們只有一個	today they say four . we don't have one . we only have one .
發生了什麼 ? 我是說 , 這裡的問題是 , 我們在這裡或許可稱為地球上有史以來最有智慧的生命有著非凡的大腦能夠運用這些ted會議上闡述備至的這些技術但我們卻在毀壞著這個惟一的家園	what happened ? i mean , the question here is , we may call it the most intelligent life on earth , perhaps the most intelligent brain of all time , with extraordinary brains that have been able to use these ted talks to illustrate the equipment , but we're destroying this very neighborhood .
全球各地的原住民在做重要決定前都會坐到一起 , 然後問 " 這決定如何影響我們接下來的七代人 ? "	natives around the world , who make big decisions , are sitting together and asking , " how does this determine affect the seven generations of the rest of us ? "
今天 , 重要決定我這裡不特別談非洲而是發達世界牽涉幾百萬美元以及以及幾百萬人的重要決定卻只是問 " 這會如何影響下次股東大會 ? "	today , critical decisions i'm not talking about africa here , but i'm talking about the world in terms of the millions of dollars and the millions of people who are just asking , " how does it impact the next shareholder meeting ? "
這些決定卻影響非洲	these decisions affect africa .
當我開始遊歷非洲談論黑猩猩面臨的問題及其日益消逝的森林我愈來愈意識到如此之多的非洲問題是如何與以前的殖民開發有關的	as i started to travel and talk about problems facing chimpanzees and their increasing forests , i became aware of how so much of africa was associated with previous colonial development .
因此我開始在非洲之外旅行 , 在歐洲演講在美國演講 , 去亞洲	so i started traveling outside africa , talking in the u . s . , going to asia .
每一地都有這些糟糕的問題	and there are these terrible questions everywhere .
你知道我說的是什麼問題 , 這包括汙染問題	you know what i mean , it includes pollution .
我們呼吸的空氣經常毒害我們	the air that we breathe constantly poisons us .
泥土毒害我們的食物	mud poisons our food .
水水也許是本世紀我們要面對的最要緊問題之一每一地 , 水都被農業、工業、家用化學制品所汙染全世界都還在噴這些製品似乎沒辦法從過去的經驗獲利	water is perhaps one of the most tense problems we have to face in this century , where water is being polluted by agriculture , industry , home chemicals , all over the world , and it seems like it's not going to be making profit from past experience .
紅樹被砍倒海嘯等影響日益加重	mangroves are increasingly affected by tsunamis , and so on .
我們談過土壤侵蝕	we talked about soil erosion .
我們不計後果地燒過化石燃料連同其它所謂溫室氣體導致了氣候變化	we've burned fossil fuels all over the consequence , and all the other socalled greenhouse gases lead to climate change .
終於 , 全世界的人都開始相信有什麼事發生了 , 我們的氣候不對勁兒了	finally , people all over the world are believing what's happening , our climate is not right .
全球氣候互相牽連	the interconnected climate is connected .
最受不利影響的是窮人	the worst impacts are the poor .
已經受影響的是非洲	it's africa .
在次撒哈拉非洲的許多地區 , 乾旱非常嚴重	drought is very serious in many parts of subsaharan africa .
雨終於下起來時 , 又常常導致洪水及更多的不幸 , 貧窮、飢餓和疾病週而復始	when the rains finally wake up , frequent flooding and more unfortunately , poverty , hunger and disease recovered .
還有很多人住在土地供養不起的地區太窮 , 買不起食物因為全部土地都剝蝕了 , 所以也沒法離開	and there's a lot of people living in land that's too poor to buy food because the land is stripped , so there's no way that you can leave .
於是有了沙漠化一點點漫延 , 漫延 , 漫延同時最後的樹也被砍倒	so we have desertification a little bit , a little bit of desertification , a little bit of desertification , a little bit of stretching ,
這種事情不光在非洲遍佈全球	it's not just that it's happening all over the world .
所以我不覺得奇怪當我在世界各地旅行時碰到那麼多年輕人 , 他們看上去失去了希望	so i don't think it's surprising that as i travel around the world , there are so many young people who seem to have lost hope .
我們似乎已經失去了智慧 , 那種屬於原住民的智慧	we seem to have lost wisdom , the indigenous wisdom of our natives .
我想問 , 這是為什麼 ?	and i wanted to ask , why is this ?
你們覺得在這異常聰明的大腦ted技術作為例證的那種大腦和人的心臟之間會有某種隔絕嗎 ? 用非科學的術語來談談根據愛和同情 。 有隔絕嗎 ?	do you think there's some kind of separation between the brain and the human heart , in an unscientific term , in terms of love and compassion ?
這些年輕人 , 當我和他們講話時基本上他們要麼情緒低落 , 要麼無動於衷或者痛苦、憤怒他們或多或少說的是同一件事情 " 我們這麼感覺是因為我們覺得你們損害了我們的未來 , 並且我們對此無能為力 。 "	these young people , when i talk to them , basically they're either emotionally low , they're either irritable or painful or angry , and they're saying more or less the same thing , " we feel that you're broken our future and we can't do anything about it . "
我們確實已經毀壞了他們的未來	we have destroyed their future .
我有三個小孫子 , 每次看著他們我就想 , 從我像他們那麼大以來 , 我們是如何損害這個美麗的地球的我感覺到這種絕望	i have three little grandchildren , and every time i look at them , i wonder how we've damaged this beautiful earth since i was as big as them , and i feel this despair .
我們由此開展這項我們稱之為 " 根與芽 " 的計劃恰好始於這裡 , 坦尚尼亞現在已經傳播到世界上97個國家	and so we launched what we call roots and shoots , which is just right here , and tanzania has now spread to 97 countries in the world .
專案的名字是具有象徵意義的根造就堅實的基礎	the name of the project is a symbolic root , which makes it solid .
芽看上去細小 , 在陽光照耀下卻可穿破磚牆	shoots look small , but under the sun they shine , it's a brick wall .
磚可以看成是我們給地球造成的環境的和社會的問題這是希望的訊息	and blocks look like the environmental and social problems we've created to the planet , and that's the message of hope .
世界各地成千上萬的年輕人可以取得突破 , 為了所有生物 , 讓這個世界更美好	hundreds and hundreds and hundreds of young people around the world have access to breakthroughs for all the creatures that make the world a better place .
" 根與芽 " 的最重要訊息每一天 , 我們每一個人都在改變世界	the most important message of roots and shoots is that every single day , every single one of us is changing the world .
我們有一個選擇這屋子裡我們每一個人我們都有一個選擇 , 關於我們想做些什麼來改變世界	we have an option for each one of us in this room , and we have a choice about what we want to do to change the world .
很窮的人沒有選擇我們要改變這些事以便窮人也有選擇	poor people don't have a choice . we have to change these things so that the poor have a choice .
" 根與芽 " 小組都選三個方案	the roots and shoots group chose three projects .
取決於成員年齡 , 所在國家在城市還是鄉下 , 來選不同的方案	depending on members of the country , on the age of the city , on the rural , to select different programs .
基本上 , 我們現在的計劃從學前一直到大學愈來愈多的成人開始建立他們自己的 " 根與芽 " 小組	essentially , we're now planning to move from school to college , and as more and more adults are starting to build their own roots and shoots .
每個小組在彼此之間選擇三種不同的方案 , 來創造更加美好的世界承認所有這些不同問題是互相聯絡彼此影響的	each group selects three different programs for each other to create a better and better world recognition that all these different problems are in contact with each other .
因此他們的方案之一將會幫助他們自己的人類社群	so one of their programs will help their own human communities .
然後 , 如果他們能幹 , 他們可以籌集資金幫助世界上其它地區的社群	and then , if they do , they can fundraise money to help communities in other parts of the world .
他們的方案之一將會幫助動物不光是野生動物也包括家養動物	one of their solutions will be to help the animals not only in wildlife , but including families .
他們的方案之一將會幫助我們共處的環境	one of their solutions will help us all live in a common situation .
交織在所有這些方案中的訊息是學著與我們自己、家庭、社群和諧相處 , 包括國家之間 , 不同文化之間不同宗教信仰之間 , 以及我們和自然世界之間	the message in all of these programs is to learn to harmonize ourselves , families , communities , between countries , different religious beliefs , and between us and the natural world .
我們需要自然世界我們不能繼續象現在這樣破壞世界了	we need the natural world , and we cannot continue to do that , to destroy the world .
我們只有一個地球	we only have one planet .
就在非洲這裡 , 僅僅選出一個或兩個 " 根與芽 " 小組正在實施的方案只要一個或兩個方案在坦尚尼亞、烏干達、肯亞、南非、剛果、布拉扎維、獅子山、喀麥隆以及別的團體 。 就象我說的 , 遍佈世界97個國家	just here in africa , you can just elect one or two roots and shoots programs that are implementing one or two programs in tanzania , uganda , kenya , southern congo , brava , sierra leone , cameroon and other groups .
當然 , 他們種樹 , 他們種有機蔬菜	of course , they plant trees , they grow organic vegetables .
他們在難民營養小雞賣雞蛋得些微薄收入或只是把雞蛋給家人吃並覺得自豪和獲得權力因為他們自己種植蔬菜養殖小雞就不再無助 , 不再依賴他人	they sell chicken eggs in refugee nutrients , either they eat chicken eggs or eat eggs for their families and feel proud and in power , because they grow their vegetables and farm their own chickens helpless no longer depend on others .
這個方案在烏干達實施了給予前童軍一些心理上的幫助	this program implemented a psychological help for the former child soldiers in uganda .
實施這些方案讓他們重塑自我	implementing these programs allows them to reinvent themselves .
再一次 , 他們成為社會上的有用一員	and again , they become members of society .
我們也在監獄實施該計劃	we also implemented the program in prison .
所以現在沒時間實施更多的 " 根與芽 " 計劃	so there's no time to do more roots and shoots .
哦 , 他們也致力於艾滋病及其病毒方面的工作	oh , they also work on hiv/aids and their viruses .
那是 " 根與芽 " 計劃非常重要的組成部分由大孩子跟小孩子談話	that's a really important component of roots and shoots , and it's made up of big kids talking to kids .
還有無意懷孕及類似事情年輕人更願意聽別的孩子的 , 而不是成人的	there's unintended pregnancy and things like young people are more likely to hear other kids than to be adults .
希望 。 我周遊世界被問及的就是這個問題 " 珍 , 你見過這麼多可怕的事情 , 你看著你的黑猩猩數量在減少 , 從世紀之交的大約一百萬到現在的不足15萬 。 那麼多其它動物也一樣	hope . what i've been asking around the world around me is this question: " jane , you've seen so many terrifying things , you've been seeing your chimpanzees decrease , you've gone from about a million to about 150 , 000 other animals through the rest of the century .

藝術家戴安娜•科恩分享關於塑膠汙染對大海和我們日常生活嚴重影響的事實和一些想法 , 幫助大家來擺脫塑膠包圍圈 。	diana cohen shares the fact that plastic pollution has a huge impact on the sea and some of the ideas that we have in our daily lives , helping people to get out of the plastic bags .
consumerism , globalissues , green , missionblue , oceans , plastic	consumerism , the global global isis sues , green mission blue , the ocean of constituency , plastic .
戴安娜•科恩diannacohen:關於塑膠汙染的嚴峻事實	diana cohen: the harsh truth about plastic pollution .
我是個視覺藝術家 , 也是塑膠汙染聯盟的創始人之一 。	i'm a visual artist and one of the founders of the plastic pollution alliance .
過去20年 , 我一直參與塑膠包的工作 , 我藝術創作的原材料是裁製和縫合塑膠 。	for the last 20 years , i've been working on plastic bags , and my artistic raw materials are tailored and sutured plastic .
讓塑膠變為平面和立體型藝術 , 雕塑和藝術裝置 。	it turns plastic into flat and threedimensional art , sculpture and art installation .
在與塑膠打交道的八年之後 , 我的一些作品開始開裂碎成許多小塑膠塊 。	eight years after dealing with plastic , some of my works began to break into little blobs of plastic .
我想 , " 好極了 。	and i thought , " great .
塑膠就像我們人類一樣短命 。 "	plastic is like us . "
我自學進一步深入瞭解塑膠 , 我的確瞭解到塑膠是個壞材料 。	i taught myself about plastic , and i did understand that plastic was a bad material .
塑膠碎成許多小塊 , 但它還是塑膠 , 這很糟糕 。	plastics are broken up into lots of little bits , but it's still plastic , which is terrible .
我們發現有很多塑膠漂浮於大海 。	we found a lot of plastic floating in the ocean .
然而在過去的幾年 , 我知道太平洋垃圾環流和垃圾漩渦 。	but for the last few years , i've known about pacific garbage patch and trash gyres .
我第一反應--我想這也是多數人的第一反應 , 知道這之後-- " 喔 , 我的上帝 !	my first response and i think that's the first response to most people , knowing that after , " oh , my god !
我們要去那裡並清理這些塑膠 。 "	we're going to go there and clean up the plastic . "
所以我提議一隻貨船 , 兩隻退役拖網漁船 , 一臺起重機 , 一臺削片機和一臺冷壓機出海 。	so i proposed a cargo ship , two decommissioned trawler , a heavy machine , a film machine and a cold presser .
我計劃是航行到垃圾環流帶 , 提高對於此汙染的高度重視 , 開始回收塑膠 , 切割它變成小片 , 然後冷壓變成塑膠塊 , 它可能被用來作為欠發達社群的建築材料 。	my plan was to voyage to the garbage dumpsters , to raise the height of the pollution , to begin to recycle plastic , cut it into small , compressed into plastic , and it might be used to escape the building materials of the community .
我同那些曾去過垃圾環流帶的人們談過 , 他們也曾研究過塑膠汙染對海洋環境的汙染 , 交談之後 , 我開始意識到海上清理塑膠相比起全球每天產生塑膠的生產量就如大海撈針一樣 , 我必須回過頭想想 , 要展望更大的藍圖 。	as i've talked about people who've been to the garbage dumpsters , who've looked at plastic pollution in the ocean environment , and after talking , i've begun to realize that plastic is as geologically generated as a global needle for generating plastic , and i have to step back and look at it and look at a bigger blueprint .
真正的解決辦法就是:我們需要在源頭找到解決方法 。	the real solution is that we need to find solutions at the source .
我們需要切斷一次性使用塑膠和一次性塑膠的源頭 , 使得它們在全球範圍內每天不會再進入大海 。	we need to cut the source of onetime plastic and oneoff plastic so that they don't enter the sea every day on a global scale .
看看這個 , 我也知道我非常生氣 。	look at this , and i know i'm very angry .
我並不只關心你也可能想象到的在太平洋中部我們現在所知的 , 權威資料是 , 11個垃圾塑膠環流帶 , 遍及世界五大海洋 。	i'm not just concerned about what you might think of , but what we now know in the middle of the pacific , where authority data is , you know , 11 garbage loops in the world through five oceans .
我不僅僅是關心塑膠環流帶 , 也包括超市的塑膠包圍圈 。	i'm not just concerned about the plastic rings but also the plastic surroundings of the supermarkets .
我要去超市 , 所有事物都是塑膠包裝 。	i'm going to the supermarket , and everything is packaged .
所有飲料都是塑膠包裝 , 甚至健康的有機市場 。	all of the beverages are plastic packaging and even the healthy organic markets .
我也關注在冰箱的塑膠 , 還有塑膠以及濾取塑膠的毒素被我們吃下和吸收到我們身體裡 。	i'm also looking at plastic in the refrigerator , and the toxins that filter plastic and get those plastics are eating and absorbing into our bodies .
我和其他的一群人們都關注這個塑膠汙染問題 , 組建了塑膠汙染聯盟 。	i and a bunch of other people focused on this plastic pollution problem , and they built the plastic pollution coalition .
我們為解決這問題開始許多活動 , 它們中的一些是非常簡單的 。	we've started many activities to solve this problem , and some of them are very simple .
其中一個是:在大海 , 我們發現百分80到百分90海洋廢棄物是塑膠 , 然後我們為什麼不稱其為:	one is that in the ocean , we find 80 to 90 percent of marine waste is plastic , and why don't we call it plastic ?
再迴圈 。 關於可持續和再迴圈的環保想法的書籍都是類似的觀點 。	again , books about sustainable and recyclable environmental ideas are similar perspectives .
大家扔東西到垃圾桶裡 , 但是從來沒有再想過此事 。	people throw things in trash cans , but never think about it again .
現實是什麼呢 ?	what is reality ?
在美國 , 塑膠垃圾回收率少於百分之七 。	plastic waste rate is less than seven percent in the united states .
大家想實際看看 , 特別當塑膠變成塑膠瓶 , 絕大多數塑膠瓶僅被降級回收 , 或者焚燒 , 或運到中國 。	people actually think that plastic becomes plastic bottles , and the vast majority of plastic bottles are being recycled or incinerated or shipped to china .
當一個塑膠瓶可以被重製成一個塑膠瓶 , 或者重被使用時 , 正是被降級回收 , 使得塑膠瓶被製成小塑膠體 , 使得一個塑膠瓶不再被製成塑膠瓶回收利用 。	when a plastic bottle can be reclaimed into a plastic bottle or reused , it's been recycled by a recycling of a plastic bottle that can be made into small plastic bottles that no longer recycled into plastic bottles .
對我們而言 , 這是個重大問題 。	it's a big problem for us .
我們關注 , 並讓人們思考的另一件事是我們在原本3個r原則前 , reduce、reuse、recycle , 加了第四個r原則 , 它就是拒絕使用 。	another thing that we've been looking at and making people think is that we redressed uce , reuse , recycle , and recycle , the fourth rprinciple of r , which is rejection .
無論何時 , 拒絕使用一次性使用塑膠和即丟塑膠 。	whenever you refuse to use oneoff plastic and disposable plastic .
有替代品的使用 。 其中一些是非常老套 。	there are alternatives . some of them are very oldfashioned .
我自己現在收集這些很酷的耐熱玻璃容器 , 使用這些而替換高興派和特百惠派塑膠容器來儲存食物 。	i myself am now collecting these cool , heated glass vessels that use these to replace the emerging parties and the charismatic plastic vessels to store food .
我知道我這樣做有利於我自己和我的家庭 。	i knew i was doing it for my own family and for my own .
我們選擇使用不鏽鋼瓶和玻璃瓶是很容易的 , 你如果要出門 , 記得帶不鏽鋼瓶 , 讓它灌滿水 , 或者濾過水 , 而不要購買塑膠瓶裝水 。	we choose not to use rustless steel bottles and glass bottles that are easy , and if you want to get out the door , you remember the stainless steel bottle that's filling it up or filtering it over the water instead of the plastic bottle
我猜我想要告訴大家的是我知道你們大家關於此塑膠汙染知道得很多漂在大海上的塑膠是個嚴重的問題 , 但這是我們做為消費者自身產生的問題 , 我們也能自身解決這問題 。	and i guess what i'd like to tell you is that i know that you all know about this plastic pollution that a lot of plastic on the sea is a serious problem , but it's a problem that we're having as consumers , and we can solve it ourselves .
我們透過提高這問題的意識 , 教導人們選擇可替換性產品 , 能夠解決這問題 。	we've taught people by raising the awareness of the question that choices are replacable , that this problem can be solved .
所以無論何時 , 請選擇使用可替換性產品 , 拒絕使用一次性使用塑膠和即丟塑膠 。	so whenever you're choosing to use alternative products , you refuse to use onetime plastic and throw plastic .

這些元件跟我口袋中的手機進行通訊 , 手機作為一個通訊和計算的裝置 。	these elements communicate with my phone in my pocket , as a communication and computational device .

我有一位葡萄牙朋友 , 其祖父用一輛腳踏車和一臺洗衣機改裝成一輛汽車供家人乘用 。	i have a friend in portugal whose grandfather converted to a bike and a washing machine and an automobile for families .
他這樣做 , 一是因為他買不起車 , 但更重要的是因為他知道如何改裝汽車 。	he did this because he couldn't afford a car , but more importantly because he knew how to change a car .
曾經 , 我們都懂得一些機械的工作原理 , 也知道它們是怎麼製造出來的 , 所以我們能夠自己製作和維修它們.或者至少基於我們的瞭解作出明智的購買決定 。	it used to be that we all understood the principles of mechanical work and how they were made , and so we could make them ourselves , or at least based on our understanding of wise purchasing decisions .
但我們很多這些diy的實用性技能在20世紀的下半葉就流失了 。	but a lot of these diy practical skills have gone missing in the lower part of the 20th century .
但是現在 , 製作者社群和開放資源模式正在把這些物品的工作原理和製造材料的知識帶回到我們的生活中 。 而且我相信我們需要把這些知識帶到下一個層面 , 也就是了解構成這些物品的元件 。	but now , the producer community and the opensource approach is bringing the principles of these objects and the knowledge of the materials that make them back into our lives , and i believe we need to bring that knowledge to the next level , which is to understand the components that make these objects .
我們很多人都知道 , 像紙和織物這樣的傳統材料是什麼做成的 , 以及它們是如何生產的 。	many of us know what traditional materials like paper and fabric are made of , and how they're made .
但是現在我們有了一些令人驚歎的未來複合材料-如可以變形的塑膠、可以導電的油漆、可以變色的顏料和可以發光的織物 。	but now we have some amazing future composites plastic , which can conduct electricity , paints that can change color , fabrics that can glow .
下面讓我們來看一些新材料 。	so let's look at some new materials .
這種導電墨水可讓我們 , 拋棄傳統的印刷電路板或電線的方法而直接用導電墨水來畫電路板 。	this conductive ink can take us away from the traditional printed circuit boards or the wires and directly draw the board directly from the conductive ink .
比如我手裡拿著的這個小裝置 , 是我們用導電墨水做成一個觸控性的感測器 , 一旦接觸人的皮膚 , 這個小燈就會亮起 。	so for example , this little device in my hand is made of a touch sensor using conductive ink , and once it's exposed to the skin , this little light goes on .
導電墨水已經被藝術家們應用到創作中了 , 最新的進展表明我們很快就能把它應用在鐳射印表機和鐳射筆中.	the conductive inks have been applied by artists to create the most recent progress that show that we'll soon be applied to a laser printer and a laser pointer .
這是一張泡浸過無色光漫顆粒丙烯酸的紙.	this is a piece of paper that's bathed in a colorless particle alanine .
只浸過普通丙烯酸的紙只在其邊緣周圍有漫光現象 , 而這張浸過無色光漫顆粒丙烯酸的紙 , 當我們開燈時漫光會照亮整張紙.	immersed only the regular paper has a comic phenomenon around its edge , and this one immersed the colored particle alanine acid , which illuminates the entire piece of paper when we turned on the lights .
就目前所知 , 這種材料已經被應用到室內設計和多點觸控系統兩個領域中了 。	and as far as we know , this material has been applied both interior design and multitouch systems .
而熱變色顏料在特定的溫度下會改變顏色 。	and thermal pigment changes color at certain temperatures .
我先把這張東西放到一個電熱板上溫度設定比外界溫度稍高一點然後你可以看到發生了什麼.	i'm going to put this on a board that has a slightly higher temperature taller than the outside world , and you can see what happens .
除了其它用途 , 這種材料主要用作嬰兒奶瓶的製造 。 它能告訴你什麼時候瓶裡的東西涼到可飲用的溫度 。	except for other uses , the material is mostly used as makers for baby bottles , and it can tell you when something in your bottle is cool enough to drink temperature .
這些就是我們通常所說的 " 智慧材料 " 的幾個例子 。	these are just a few examples of the intelligent materials we usually talk about .
幾年內 , 它們將被應用到很多我們日常使用的物件和科技產品上 。	within a few years , they will be used for many of the objects and technological products that we use every day .
我們也許還不會有科幻小說向我們保證的飛行汽車 , 但是我們能擁有隨溫度變色的牆 , 可以捲起來的鍵盤 , 和一<unk>開關就變不透明的窗戶 。	we may not have science fiction yet to assure us flying cars , but we can have walls that are colored with temperature , keyboards that are rolling up , and those that are meant to turn out to be transparent .
我是科班出身的社會科學家 , 為什麼今天我在這裡講智慧材料 ?	i'm a social scientist in coban , and why am i here talking about smart materials ?
首先 , 我是個製造者 。	first of all , i'm a maker .
我對於東西如何運轉和怎樣製作有好奇心 , 我也相信我們應該對我們這個世界的組成材料有更深的瞭解 , 並且現在 , 我們對於這些構成我們未來的高科技材料瞭解不多 。	i'm curious about how things work and how they work , and i'm convinced that we should have a deeper understanding of the materials that make up our world , and right now , we don't know a lot about these hightech materials that make up our future .
要獲得少量的智慧材料是很難的 。	it's hard to get a small amount of smart material .
有關如何使用這些材料的資訊也很少 , 它們是如何製作的資訊就更加少得可憐 。	there's very little information about how you're using these materials , and they're making even less miserable information about how you're using them .
目前 , 它們絕大多數都存在於貿易機密和專利中 , 只有大學和大公司才能得到 。	right now , the overwhelming majority of them exist in trade secrets and patents that only have universities and big companies .
所以三年多以前 , 我和kirstyboyle發起了一個叫做openmaterials的專案 。	so a little over three years ago , kirstyboyle and i started a project called open materials .
在那個網站上 , 我們和想要加入我們的任何人 , 分享實驗 , 釋出資訊 , 鼓勵其他人為此作出力所能及的貢獻 , 並且收集像研究論文和像我們一樣的製造者所製作的教程一類的資源 。	on that website , we and anyone who wants to join us , share experiments , encourage others to make a contribution to this , and collect resources like research papers made of manufacturers just like us .
我們希望把這一網站做成一個大規模的、集體生成的資料庫 , 蒐集用智慧材料diy的資訊 。	we wanted to take this website and make a largescale , collectively generated database and gather information about smart materials , diy materials .
但是我們為什麼要關心智慧材料是如何工作和它們是用什麼來製造的呢 ?	but why should we care about how intelligent materials work and what do they build with them ?
首先 , 因為我們無法影響我們不理解的東西 , 我們不理解和不會用的東西還會反過來影響我們 。	first , because we can't influence things we don't understand , we don't understand and use things that don't work the other way around .
我們使用的東西 , 我們穿的衣服 , 我們住的房子 , 都對我們的行為、健康和生活質量上產生深遠的影響 。	the things we use , the clothes we we use , the houses we live in have a profound impact on our actions , our health and quality of life .
所以如果我們將要生活在一個由智慧材料構成的世界中 , 我們就應該知道並瞭解它們 。	so if we're going to live in a world made of smart materials , we should know and understand them .
第二 , 同樣重要地 , 創新總是來源於修補匠 。	secondly , just as importantly , innovation always comes from fixing the makers .
很多時候 , 是業餘愛好者而非專家 , 發明和改進了諸如山地車、半導體、個人電腦、甚至飛機 。	most of the time , hobbyists and experts , inventions and improvements things like mountain vehicles , semiconductors , personal computers , and airplanes .
材料科學的最大挑戰是它的複雜性 , 以及對昂貴的儀器的需求 。	the biggest challenge of material science is its complexity and its demand for expensive equipment .
但事實並非總如此 。	but that's not always the case .
伊利諾伊大學的兩名科學家在他們發表一篇關於用更簡便的方法制作導電墨水的論文時就明白了這個道理 。	two scientists at the university of illinois understood this when they wrote a paper about conducting electricity inks in a simpleer way .
jordanbunker在這一實驗之前是一個沒有任何化學經驗的人 。 他讀了這篇論文後在他的工作間裡用現成的物質和工具重複了這個實驗 。	and jordanbunker , who didn't have any chemistry at all , reading this essay , repeated the experiment with the present matter and tools in his work .
他用了一個烤箱 , 而且他甚至在另一個科學家/製造者的教程的基礎上自制了旋渦混合器 。	he used a oven , and he even made himself a turbine mixer on another scientist , from another maker .
後來 , jordan在網上發表了他的實驗結果 , 包括所有他試過的沒成功的東西 , 這樣其他人可以學習然後複製這一實驗 。	and then , jordan published his experiment online , including all the unsuccessful things he had tried so that others could learn and copy the experiment .
所以jordan主要創新方式是拿一個在設施齊全的大學實驗室裡創造的實驗 , 然後在芝加哥的一個車庫裡用便宜材料和自制的工具來重複實驗 。	so jordan's main innovation was to take an experiment that was created in a university laboratory in order to repeat it in a garage in chicago with cheap materials and autonomous tools .
在他發表的實驗結果基礎上 , 其他人可以接著做下去並且設計甚至更簡單的步驟和改進實驗 。	and based on the experimental results he published , others can then do it and design simpler steps and improvements .
我想分享的另外一個例子她專案的目標是在突出材料富有表現力的特質的同時專注於製造者的創造力和製造技巧 。	another example i want to share with you is that her goal is to highlight the quality of the materials that express the quality of the expressive quality and the creative skills of the maker .
電子工具在教我們東西如何運轉這方面非常有力 , 但是它們設計中傳承下來的約束影響我們學習的方式 。	electronic tools are teaching us very powerful in how things work , but the restrictions that they have inherited in their design impact the way we learn .
所以hannah的方法 , 在另一方面 , 就是創制一系列的技術 , 來創造非常規的東西 , 透過教給我們材料本身的知識 , 把我們從事先設計好的約束中解放出來 。	so the hannah approach , on the other hand , is to create a series of technologies to create really regular things by teaching us the knowledge of the material itself , to free us from predesigned constraints .
在hannah眾多令人欽佩的試驗中 , 這個是我的最愛之一 。	this is one of my favorites in the most impressive trials in hannah .
[ " 會說話的紙 " ]我們在這裡看到的只不過是一張紙上面的銅帶連線著一個mp3播放器和一塊磁鐵 。	[ " paper of speaking " ] what we're seeing here is just a piece of paper that has a copper tape attached to it with an mp3 player and a magnet .
在麻省理工學院教授marcelocoelho研究的基礎上 , hannah使用各種材料創造了一系列紙質揚聲器 。 從普通的銅帶到導電的織物和墨水 ,	on the basis of marcelo coelho's studies at mit , hannah created a series of paper speakers using materials , from ordinary copper to conductive fabric and ink .
就像jordan和其他很多製造者一樣 , hannah發表了她的配方並且允許任何人來重複這些實驗 。	as jordan and many other makers , hannah published her recipe and allowed anyone to repeat these experiments .
但是紙上電子是材料科學中最有前景的分支之一 , 因為它讓我們能創造出便宜又靈活的電子產品 。	but paper electronics is one of the most promising branches of material science , because it allows us to create cheap , flexible electronics .
所以hannah的手工作品 , 和她分享了她的發現這個事實 , 打開了一扇門 , 通向兼具美學和創新的一系列新的可能 。	so hannah's hand product shared with her her discovery that opened the door to a new set of new possibilities for both aesthetic and innovation .
製造者的有趣之處在於我們創造是出於熱情和好奇 , 並且我們不害怕失敗 。	what's interesting about makers is that we create things that are passionate and curious , and we're not afraid of failure .
我們通常從非傳統的角度處理問題 , 並且 , 在這個過程中 , 最終發現其他方案或者更好的方法 。	we deal with problems from an unconventional perspective , and in the process , we find other alternatives or better ways .
所以當更多的人願意用新材料做試驗的時候 , 更多的研究者就會願意分享他們的研究成果 ; 有更多的製造商分享他們的知識 , 我們就會有更好的機會來創造造福我們所有人的科技 。	so when more people are willing to experiment with new materials , more researchers are willing to share their work ; more manufacturers are sharing their knowledge , we have better opportunities to create technologies that benefit all of us .
我的感覺有一點像tednelson在70年代初期的感覺一樣 , 他寫道 , " 你們現在必需懂電腦 。 "	i feel a little bit like tednelson in the early '70s , who wrote , " you need to understand computers now . "
那個時候 , 電腦是這些只有科學家關心的大型機 , 沒有人會夢想到放一臺在家裡 。	at the time , the computer was these big machines only scientists care about , and nobody dreamed of going home .
所以我今天站在這裡說 " 你們現在必需懂智慧材料 " 有一點奇怪 。	so i'm standing here today and saying , " you need to understand smart materials . "
請記住對於新興科技擁有先發制人的知識是確保我們在對未來的創造中有發言權的最好方式 。	bear in mind that the preemptive knowledge of emerging technology is the best way to make sure that we have a say in the future .
當我們開車是 , 我們就坐進了一個玻璃氣泡中 , 鎖上門 , 踩下油門 , 依靠眼睛為我們自己導航 。 即使我們僅僅只能看見車前車後的幾輛車 。 但是假如汽車能互換關於位置、速度的資料 , 並運用預測模型來為每一位司機測算最安全的線路呢 ? 詹妮佛海麗構想了一個零車禍的世界 。	and as we drive , we sit in a glass bubble , lock the gas door , press the gas door , navigate it with our eyes , even though we can only see a few cars behind the train , but what if the cars were able to exchange information about location , speed , and use the model to predict the safest course for each driver ?
詹妮弗海麗:汽車若能交流車禍或可避免	jennifer haley: cars can talk to traffic vehicles or avoid .
讓我們來面對一樁事實吧開車是一件危險的事	let's face it , driving is a dangerous thing .
它是我們不願意去想的事物之一但事實上那些神像和平安符世界各地都有人把它們擺在儀表盤的上方這就無意中透露出一個我們都心知肚明的事實	it's one of the things that we don't want to think about , but in fact , the gods are peacefully peaceful and accomplished all over the world , people are putting them on top of the table , and it reveals an unintended fact that we
車禍是死亡的主因尤其在美國16到19歲的美國人群中死亡的主因並且百分之七十五的車禍都與毒品和酒精無關	car accidents are the cause of death , especially in the united states between the ages of 16 and 19 , and 75 percent have nothing to do with drugs and alcohol .
沒人能給出確切答案但我記得我第一次出車禍	no one can give an exact answer , but i remember the first time i had a car accident .
我當時還是個開車的新手 , 當時正在外面高速路上開著車 。 我突然看見我前面汽車的剎車燈亮了	i was driving , and i was driving , and i was driving along the way , and all of a sudden i saw the brakes in front of my car .
我當時想好吧他減速了那我也減速好了	and i thought , okay , he speeds up , and i'll slow down .
我踩了剎車	i had stepped on the brakes .
但是我前面那個人並不是在減速	but the guy in front of me is not slowing down .
他停車了突然停車在高速路上突然停車	he stopped the truck , and all of a sudden , stopped on the freeway .
速度從65邁瞬降到0	it goes from 65 to zero .
我猛踩剎車	i cracked on the brakes .
我當時感覺到我的車的防抱死系統啟動了但車還在行駛並沒停下來的意思我也知道我的車停不了了安全氣囊也鼓了起來車報廢了但幸運的是沒有人受傷	i felt like my car's defense system was launched , but the car was still moving , and i knew that my car stopped , and that airbags were supposed to be injured , but fortunately nobody was hurt .
但我根本不知道我前面那輛車要停而且我想我們可以比那做得更好	but i didn't know that i was going to park in front of me , and i think we can do better than that .
我想我們透過實現 " 讓汽車之間對話 " 來改變我們的駕駛體驗	i think we can change our driver's experience by releasing the conversation between the cars .
我希望你們能思考片刻思考一下現在的駕駛體驗是怎麼樣的	i want you to think for a moment about what the experience of the driving experience looks like .
坐進車裡關上車門你就已經置身在一個玻璃氣泡中	you're sitting in your car and you're closing your door , and you're already in a glass bubble .
你不能直接感受到你周圍的世界	you can't just feel the world around you .
因為你坐在車這樣一個不小的空間裡	because you're sitting in a slightly small space .

對吧 ? 你只能靠雙眼來導航	right ? you can only navigate with your eyes .
對你別無他法眼睛並非是用來幹著活兒的但是有些事情你就必須得做 , 比方說 , 你想換個車道那你第一件要做的事是什麼	it's not about having eyes for you , it's not about having a survival , but there are things you have to do , for example , you want to change your lanes , so what do the first thing that you do ?
將眼睛從車道上移開對	remove the eyes from the driveway .
將目光從你前進的方向移開轉彎檢查一下盲點然後就一直開根本不注意自己在往哪裡開	shifting your eyes from the direction you're moving in , checking the bend of the blind spots , and just keeping your eyes on where you're going .
所有人都這麼做這是安全的駕駛方式	and everybody else does it , and it's a safe way of driving .
我們為什麼這麼做 ? 因為我們別無選擇我們必須作出一個抉擇是朝這兒看還是朝那兒看	why do we do this ? because we have no choice , and we have to make a decision , and we have to look at it or look at it .
我們通常都做得很好能夠很好的選擇我們要往哪個方向開	we're usually pretty good at choosing where we're going in a direction .
但是偶然我們也會忘記一些事情	but incidentally , we forget a few things .
有時當我們發覺有些東西出了問題的時候已經為時過晚 。	sometimes when we find something wrong , it's already too late .

但是現存的科技可以幫我們改善這一點	but existing technologies can help us improve this .
在未來車與車之間可以交換資料我們就不僅只能看見前面的三臺車了還能看見後面的三臺車 , 左邊的 , 以及右邊車 。 同時看見鳥瞰視野我們可以看見這些車的內部	we can exchange data between the cars in the future , and we can see not only the three cars in the front , but also the three cars in the back , the one on the left , and the car on the right , and we can see bird's eye view of the car .
我們可以看到我們前面那輛車的速度看看前面那位什麼時候會啟動或停下	we can see the velocity in front of us , and look at the vehicle in front of us , when the seat in front of you is activating or stopping .
假如那人的速度突然降到零 , 我就能知道了 。	if the speed of the person is crashing down to zero , i can see .
利用運算代數以及預測模型我們能看見未來	with algorithms and predictive models , we can see the future .
你可能會覺得這是不可能的	you might think that's impossible .
你怎麼能預測未來呢太難了	how can you predict the future ?
事實上不難對於汽車來說這並非不可能	in fact , it's not that hard for cars to say it's not impossible .
汽車是三維物體位置速度都是固定的	the automobile is a threedimensional object fixed by speed .
行使在路上的時候	it's in the middle of the road .
它們通常都是按照預先規劃好的道路行駛	they're usually traffic roads according to preprocessing .
未來想要預測汽車將要駛向什麼方向對之作出合理的預測並不困難	it's not hard to predict where cars are headed in the future .
即使你在自己的車裡突然出現了一個開著摩托的人砰 ! 時速85英里 , 跟你搶車道我知道你們曾經有過這樣的經歷那個開摩托的並非憑空出現	even if you had suddenly seen a motorcycle in your car , boom ! 85 miles an hour , ride with your lane , i know you've had that experience with that moto , and it didn't come out of the void .
他可能之前的半小時就一直在路上開著吧	he may have been driving for half an hour before , right ?
對吧 ? 我的意思是 , 有人看見過他	right ? i mean , somebody's seen him .
在10 , 20 , 30英里前 , 有人看見過他 , 只要一輛車看見那個人將他的資訊置入地圖中 , 他的位置就會顯示在地圖上了位置 , 速度預測他將保持85英里的時速	and 10 , 20 , 30 miles ago , someone saw him , just seeing the car seeing the person putting his information in the map , and his position shows its position in the map and predicting the speed at which he will remain 85 miles an hour .

你可以對汽車的運動作出合理的預測 。	you can make reasonable predictions about the motion of a car .
它們可是遵從牛頓力學的物體	they're newtonian objects .

王鮑勃教授和他的團隊做了個電腦模擬系統來研究當我們結合不同的模糊預測的時候會發生什麼即使只是在交通情況通暢、汽車僅僅共享gps資料時之後我們讓這項研究不僅限於電腦模擬我們還用機器人測試床它們用到的感測器正是當下汽車裡真正在用到的感測器在這些機器人上有立體相機gps二位鐳射測距儀這些都是備用系統中非常常見的	and professor bob and his team built a computer simulation system to study what happens when we combine different ambiguities , and even after sharing gps data just to share gps data , we enabled this research not just to simulate computer simulations , but to test beds for sensors that are actually using these robots , and we're using these laser stereotyping sensors that are actually using these robots , gps , and these laser pins , these are using very common systems .

問題之一就是當 " 悄悄話 " 太氾濫就很難處理所有的資訊所以你必須抓重點在這樣的情況下預測模型就可以派上用場了	one of the problems is that when a whisper is too epidemic , it's very hard to process all the information , so you have to focus on predictive models like this , and you can use them .

我認為這是一個非常令人不安的想法設想我們自己的車將要監視著我們跟其他的車分享我們的一舉一動那樣我們就像開車穿過對我們指指點點的人群	i think it's a very uncomfortable idea to think that our own cars are going to spy on our own vehicles , sharing our actions with other cars , and that we're driving across people who point to us .

貝基布蘭頓計劃在一年裡就在他的小貨車裡住並且遊歷全國 , 但是當沮喪加劇而且自由作家的工作泡湯的時候 , 他的旅營就變成了無家可歸了 。 在這個溫馨的演講中 , 她描述了她作為美國無家可歸的工作者之一的獨特經歷 。	so beckie brandon was living in his van for a year and traveling across the country , but when it was depressed and freely authorized , his journey became homeless , and in this wonderful speech , she described the unique experience of being a homeless worker in america .

貝基布蘭頓:我無家可歸的一年	beckie brandon: a year of homelessness .
我是一個作家 , 一個新聞記者 , 我也是一位具有強烈求知慾的人 。 所以在做新聞記者的22年裡 , 我知道了很多新奇的事物 。	i'm a writer , and i'm a journalist , and i'm an incredibly inquisitive person , so for 22 years , working as a journalist , i know a lot of new things .
而三年前 , 我學會做的一件事就是變成隱形人 。	and one of the things i learned three years ago was to become invisible .
我成了一個無家可歸的工作者 。	i became a homeless worker .
我辭掉了報紙編輯的工作在我父親那年二月去世之後我決定去旅行	i quit my newspaper editor's job , and after my father died in february of that year , i decided to travel .
他的去世對我打擊非常大 。	his death struck me very much .
當時這麼做 , 是因為有很多我想去感知和處理的事 。	and this was because there were a lot of things i wanted to perceive and process .

所以 , 我就帶上我的貓 , 我的羅特威爾犬和露營的裝備裝載到1975產的雪佛萊旅遊車上 , 開車去看日落但當時完全沒想過三件嚴重的事	so i took my cat , my rottwell and camp equipment , uploaded to the 1975 schevley vehicle , drove to sunset and didn't even think of three serious things .
一:社會將住房即使是很小的房間 , 和人的價值等同起來 。	one: society will live in a small room as much as the value of a person .
二:我沒有意識到其他人的負面言語對我們本身的影響是多麼嚴重 , 假如我們放任不管 。	two: i didn't realize how severe the negative language of others affected us if we let go of it .
三:我沒有意識到無家可歸是一種生活態度而不是一種生活方式 。	three: i didn't realize that homelessness was a lifestyle as a lifestyle as a lifestyle .
一開始 , 住在車裡是很不錯的 。	and at first , it was great to live in a car .
我在露天洗澡 , 正常的去外面吃東西 。	i was on the opening day , and i was taking my baths , and i was eating normally .
而且有時間去抒發情感 。	and there's time to ly on the emotions .
但是後來 , 因我父親去世而帶來的悲憤和痛沮開始加劇 。	but then , the grief and depression started to appear as my father died .
我自由作家的工作結束了 。 我就需要去找一件全職工作來支付我的賬單 。	my free writer's job ended . i had to go find a fulltime job to pay my bills .
從一個非常溫和的春天變到一個極其炎熱的夏天會怎樣呢 。	from a very mild spring to a very hot summer of its inflammation .
不管車停在哪都是難以忍受的不用說也很明顯我帶著一隻貓和一隻狗 , 而且非常的熱 。	it's hard to endure anywhere , and it's obvious to me to carry a cat and a dog , and it's very hot .
貓從車窗來回的跑 。	cats came back from windows .

在夜裡車裡的溫度很少會降到華氏80度以下 , 這使我幾乎無法入睡 。	the temperature of the car in the night would rarely fall below 80 degrees fahrenheit , and it made me almost impossible to sleep .
食物在高溫下腐壞 。	food rotten in the heat .

當冬天來臨的時候 , 溫度驟降到零度以下 。 然後就一直這麼冷 。	when winter came , the temperature came below zero degrees , and it stayed so cold .

我也不知道什麼時候或者是如何發生的 , 我這麼快就從一個有才的寫手 , 新聞從業者變成一個無家可歸 , 住在車裡的女人這簡直是快的難以置信 。	i don't know when or how it happened , soon i went from being a talented writer to being a homeless woman , a woman living in the car , and it was incredibly rapid .

我只是沒有喝醉或者興奮 。	i'm just not drunk or excited .
當一些無家可歸的人意識到 , 包括一個以前在大學任教的教授 , 他們說: " 你不是無家可歸 , 你真正在這裡的原因是什麼 ? "	when several homeless people realized that , including a professor who'd been teaching at university , they said , " why aren't you homeless ? "
其他的無家可歸的人不把我當作是無家可歸的人看待 。 但是我自己是這麼認為的 。	other homeless people don't see me as homeless people , but i do .

真正無家可歸的人並沒有希望可言 。 "	the real homeless person is not hoping for it . "

在tedxchange系列中 , 泰國的 " 安全套之父 " , mechaiviravaidya向觀眾展示泰國在二十世紀七十年代如何採取大膽的措施來提高人民的生活水平 。 控制人口是他們的首要任務 。 他的演講圍繞安全套展開 , 直爽風趣 , 也發人深省 。	in the tedxchange series , the father of thailand's " the father of the condom , " mechaivia ivaidya shows audiences how thailand was taking audacious measures in the 1970s to improve people's lives . the control of populations was the number one thing that they needed to do .

我們開始推行計劃生育政策 , 採取了一套非常成功的母子保健措施 , 多項措施 。	we started planning for fertility policy , and we took a very successful set of female healthcare measures , multiple measures .
總的來說 , 如果孩子出生後不能存活 , 自然不會有人接受計劃生育 。	anyway , if a child is born without survival , then there's not going to be a planned birth .
所以 , 第一步就要保證孩子和母親的生活 , 然後實行計劃生育 。	so the first step is to guarantee the life of the child and the mother , and to implement planned reproduction .

在美國除了紐約展覽廳沒有博物館或展覽廳會展示波特羅的作品他們沒有膽量展示這些繪畫因為繪畫主題是關於阿布格萊布監獄	in the united states , there are no museums or galleries in the u . s . , and there's no gut about presenting these drawings , because theme is about the abu ghraib prison .

規則常常發生變化 , 但總是對男性有益就這樣 , 在一致遵循的狀況下在經濟上並不成立的規則卻完美地存在	the rules are constantly changing , but they always benefit the men , and in the consensus , the rules are perfectly occurring perfectly .

我再也受不了少數人操縱多數人透過性別 , 收入 , 種族和階級的手段	i couldn't manipulate the vast majority of people through gender , income , race and class strategies .

讓我們走出冷氣房 , 捲起袖子開始行動 , 帶著我們的熱情創造一個近乎完美的世界	let's get out of the cold , roll up our sleeves , start to act , take our passion to create an almost perfect world .
在一個倫敦那麼大的城市裡 , 每天都要消耗掉三千萬噸糧食 。 但是 , 這些食物都從何而來 ? 建築師carolynsteel探討每天餵養一個城市的神話 , 介紹古代的食物運輸如何影響城市的形成和發展 。	in a city the size of london , they consume 30 million tons of food every day , but where does it come from ? an architect carolyn steel explores the mythology of a city every day , introducing how ancient food transport affects the formation and development of the city .
cities , culture , food , globalissues	you're good , you're good , you're good , you're good .

如何餵養一個城市 ?	how do you feed a city ?

我們住在每天有食物供應的城市 , 彷彿這是世界上最自然的事情 , 我們忘記了我們也是動物 , 所以我們需要進食 , 事實上我們要依賴自然界就如同我們的祖先要依賴自然界一樣 。	we live in a city with food supply , as if it's the most natural thing in the world , we forget that we are animals , so we need to eat , and in fact , we depend on our ancestors as much as our ancestors depend on the natural world .

雖然說需要3倍的糧食事實上卻是10倍的食物來餵養一個人 , 如果從餵養動物的糧食也計算在內這並不是一個很有效率的餵養方式	and while it takes three times as much food , it's actually ten times as much food as feeding a person , it's not a very efficient way to feed an animal , if you feed it from food to animals .

每年有1900萬公頃的雨林消失它們用作開墾新的耕地	19 million hectares of rainforests are disappeared every year to reclaim new farming sites .
儘管與此同時我們也失去等量的現有耕地 , 因為鹽鹼化或水土流失	in spite of that , we also lose the equivalent of existing arable land , because of saltization or soil displacement .

在歐洲 , 我們需要10卡路里的能量來生產1卡路里為我們消耗的食物	in europe , we need 10 calories of energy to produce a calorie that consumes the food we consume .

事實上 , 你可以看出食物是如何塑造一個城市的透過閱讀街道的名稱 , 你就會發現很多線索	in fact , you can see how food is shaped in a city by reading the streets , and you can see a lot of clues .

事實上 , 當你在星期日吃午飯的時候你將很有可能聽到窗外的牛羊的叫聲在三年以前	in fact , when you're eating lunch on sunday , you're likely to hear the screaming of a sheep out the window three years ago .
因此 , 顯然他是一個有機城市屬於有機迴圈中的一個部分	so , obviously , he's part of an organic city that belongs to an organic loop .
但是 , 10年後 , 一切都改變了	but , 10 years later , everything changed .
這是大西鐵路在1840的照片	this is an image of the western railway in 1840 .

一夕之間 , 這些動物不再走進市場	all of a sudden , these animals stopped walking into the market .
他們被屠宰了在鄉村的某個地方	they were slaughtered somewhere in the countryside .
然後他們透過鐵路來到了城市	and they came to the city through railroads .
這些改變了一切	and that changed everything .
首先 , 他第一次使城市成長變成了可能不論地點、成為什麼規模和形狀的城市	first of all , he enabled himself to grow cities , possibly , on the scale and shape of cities .
城市發展過去受到地理的限制城市需要透過很艱難的方式獲得食物	cities have developed past geographic constraints , and cities need to be eaten in hard ways .
突然 , 他們從地理限制中解放了出來	suddenly , they were liberated from geographic constraints .
你可以看看倫敦的地圖在鐵路建成後的90年它從容易餵飽的一小點透過動物步行到市場等方式成長成為大型的奢侈的大都市步行運輸再也不能餵飽每個人不論是對人還是對動物	if you look at the map of london , 90 years after it was built , it went from being small feeding points , from animals walking to market , to growing to large luxury urban urban operations , and then feeding nobody else , either to animals or to animals .
當然 , 這僅僅是開始 。 當汽車代替了火車這真正標誌這個過程的結束	of course , this is just the beginning . when automobiles overcome the train , the real symbol of the process .
這是城市的最終解放從自然的束縛中完全的解放了	this is the final emancipation of the city , complete liberation from the natural constraints .
這樣型別的城市沒有了原來城市的味道亂糟糟的市容 , 當然也缺少了人因為沒有人想要在這麼大的一塊地方步行	in a way , the smell of a city like this is not necessarily a bad city , and of course it's missing a lot of people , because nobody wants to walk in a place that's so big .
事實上 , 他們都開小汽車去購買食物了開車去郊外的超級市場買回來一週需要的食物然後考慮到底如何規劃這些食品	in fact , they drive little cars to buy food , drive to the supermarkets outside of the suburbs , buy the food they need for a week and think about how to plan these foods .
這時刻 , 食物和城市的關係 , 完全的改變了	this is the moment when food and urban relations completely changed .
過去買食物是在市中心在城市的最核心地帶	it used to be buying food in the center of the city , at the very heart of the city .
買賣食物曾經是一種社會性的活動 ,	buying food was a social event .
我們原來還需要烹飪 , 現在我們只需要加水或者是一些雞蛋 , 當我們在做蛋糕或者其他東西的時候	we had to cook . now we had to add water , or some chicken eggs , when we were making cakes or something .
我們不會在去聞聞食物來確認它是否可以吃了	we're not going to smell food to make sure it's okay .
我們只是閱讀包裝袋上的使用說明就好	we're just using illustrations in the package .
我們沒有發現食物的價值 , 我們也不信賴它	we don't discover the value of food , and we don't trust it .
我們甚至擔心它	we even worry about it .
從體會它的價值變成浪費	from appreciating its values to waste .
當今食品工業最最諷刺的是他們讓生活極致地便利卻也使得一切更為複雜	the most ironic thing about the food industry today is that they make everything more vigorous and more complicated .
因為可以自由的建立新城市但是他們卻疏遠了人可貴的聯絡也就是人與自然的聯絡	they were alienated by the freedom of creating new cities , but they were alienating the valuable contacts of humans and natural networks .
同時 , 他們也讓我們依賴這個系統這個系統 , 在我們看來 , 是不可持續的	and they're also allowing us to rely on this system , which is , in our case , unsustainable .
所以 , 我們應該做點什麼呢 ?	so , what are we going to do ?
這不是一個新的問題	this is not a new question .
500年前 , 湯馬斯摩爾曾經問過自己	500 years ago , thomas moore asked herself .
這是他的書《烏托邦》的主旨	this is his book , " utopia . "
它是一個半獨立的城邦如果這麼說聽上去還比較熟悉的話一天的行走你會看見所有人農場都在瘋狂的種植或者在自己的後院種植蔬菜然後一起享用鄉鎮的共有食物 , 等等	it's a semiindependent citystate , and if that sounds like it might go on a more familiar day , you'll see that everybody farms are growing crazy plants , or growing vegetables in their own backyards , and together sharing food in towns , and so on and so forth .

當仁愛憲章發起數星期後 , 卡倫•阿姆斯特朗又將目光轉向宗教在二十一世紀所扮演的角色 。 她提出: " 宗教教義是否會使我們產生分歧 ? 抑或將我們團結在一起為了共同的利益 ? 卡倫•阿姆斯特朗:重拾恕道	karen armstrom: pick up forgiveness .
多年來 , 我一直感到沮喪因為作為宗教歷史學家 , 我已經意識到世界上主要的宗教信仰都宣揚仁愛之心 。	for years , i've been frustrated because as a religious historian , i've come to realize that the majority of religions around the world celebrate compassion .
每個宗教都演變出自己獨特的版本 , 這些統稱為恕道 。	each religion has evolved its own unique version , called the golden rule .
有時從正面說 , 那就是- " 推己及人 。 "	sometimes , from the positive , it's , " selfserving and humanizing . "
同樣重要的 , 從反方面說就是-- " 已所不欲 , 勿施於人 。 "	and equally important , in terms of it , it says , " don't do to people anymore , don't do to people . "
審視你的內心 。 探尋究竟是什麼讓你痛苦 。 然後在任何情況下 , 都拒絕將這種痛苦施加於別人 。	look at your gut . look at what makes you suffer , and in any case , it refuses to impose that pain to others .
人們之所以重視仁愛 , 不僅僅是因為它聽起來很棒 , 更是因為它行得通 。	the reason that people value compassion isn't just because it sounds great , but it works because it works .
人們發現當他們遵守恕道時正如孔子所說的 " 終生行之 , " 這已不是隻做一天好事然後又回到貪婪、自私的生活的問題了 。 當你每天都堅守恕道的時候 , 你就可以擺脫以自我為中心的世界 , 超然於物外 。	it turns out that when they follow the golden rules , as confucius put it , " survive , " that's not a good thing to do a day of the day , and then back to the question of your greed and selfish life when you're every day , you can get rid of the world where you're selfcentered , transcendent to the outside .

因為世上的一些特例 , 經常的 , 當宗教人士集聚在一起的時候 , 宗教領袖聚在一起的時候 , 他們會爭辯深奧的理論或者發表充滿仇恨的言論又或譴責同性戀等此類問題 。	because oftentimes , when religious leaders come together , religious leaders come together , they'll have a deep theory or a very hatred speech or a gay question .
通常人們不具有仁愛之心 。	people don't usually have compassion .

這當然違背了修行的目的 。	of course , it's against the purpose of the amendment .

假若我們不設法在全球實施恕道 , 這樣我們就能對待所有的人 , 無論他們在哪裡 , 他們是誰 , 都如同對待我們自己一樣重要 , 我懷疑我們能否將這個世界傳承給下一代 。	if we don't do the global golden rule so that we can treat everyone where they are and who they are as important as ourselves , i doubt whether we can pass the world on to the next generation .

mit研究人員斯凱拉•蒂比茨從事自我裝配的研究一個取代建造東西的主意 , 我們能創建制作自己的材料 , 很像dna鏈打包的方式 。 目前還是一個巨大概念的早期階段 ; 蒂比茨向我們展示了三個還在實驗中的專案 , 我們可以一窺一個自我裝配的未來可能的樣子 。	mit researcher kara tibitz works on selfassembly research , an idea for building things , where we can create our own materials , much like the way the dna chains are currently in the early stages of a great concept ; tibbyzi is showing us three projects in which we can peek into a future of selfregulation .
斯凱拉•蒂比茨:我們能製作可以製作自己的東西麼 ?	skera tibitz: can we make things that we can make ourselves ?
今天我想向各位展示未來我們製作東西的方式 。	today i want to show you how we make things in the future .
我相信很快我們的建築和機器將能自我組裝 , 自我複製和自我修復 。	i believe soon our buildings and machines will selfassemble , selfreplicate and repair .
因此我要向各位展示我所認為的製造業的當前狀況 , 接著再將其與一些自然系統比較 。	so i'm going to show you what i think of as the forefront of the manufacturing industry and then compare it to some of the natural systems .
那麼在當前的製造業中 , 我們有摩天大樓兩年半的時間 , 50萬至上百萬個部分 , 非常複雜 , 使用了在鋼鐵 , 混凝土和玻璃方面的新技術 。	so in the current manufacturing industry , we have two and a half years of skyscrapers , 500 , 000 to millions of parts , very complicated , using new technologies for steel , concrete and glass .
我們有令人激動的機器 , 可以帶我們進入太空五年時間 , 兩百五十萬個部分 。	we have an exciting machine that takes us five years into space , two and a half million parts .
但另一方面 , 如果看看自然系統 , 我們有擁有兩百萬種類型的蛋白質 , 能在一萬納秒內摺疊起來 , 我們能在大約一小時內對帶有三十億鹼基對的dna進行復制 。	but on the other hand , if you look at the natural system , we have two million types of proteins that fold up in 10 , 000 nanoseconds , and we can recover in about an hour with three billion base pairs of dna .
這就是我們自然系統的複雜性 , 但它們非常高效 , 比我們建造的任何東西都要高效 , 比我們能建造的任何東西都要複雜 。	this is the complexity of our natural system , but they're very efficient , they're more efficient than anything we build , and they're more complex than anything we can build .
它們在能源方面更加高效 。	they're more energyefficient .
它們很少犯錯 。	they rarely make mistakes .
他們能自我修復保持長壽 。	they can repair themselves for longevity .
關於自然系統有件超級有意思的事情 。	there's something really interesting about the natural system .
如果我們能將其轉換為我們的建築環境 , 那麼我們構建事物的方式就會有很大的潛力 。	if we can convert this into our built environment , then there's a lot of potential for how we construct things .
我認為關鍵是自我組裝 。	i think the key is selfassembly .
如果我們想要在自身的身體環境中利用自我組裝 , 我認為有四個關鍵因素 。	if we want to use our selfassembly in our physical environment , i think there are four key factors .
第一個是 , 我們需要解碼我們所要建造的東西的所有的複雜度也就是我們的建築和機器 。	the first is that we need to decode all the complexities of the things we build , our buildings and machines .
我們需要把它們解碼成簡單的序列基本上就是我們的建築運作的dna 。	we need to decode them into simple sequences that are essentially the dna of how our buildings work .
接著我們需要可程式設計的部分這部分能接受這一序列並用於摺疊或是重塑 。	and then we need programmable parts that accept this sequence for folding and reimagining .
我們需要一些能量來進行啟用 , 使我們的這些部分能夠依照程式摺疊起來 。	we need some energy to do that so that these portions of ours can code in action .
我們需要一些型別的糾錯冗餘以保證我們成功建造的就是我們想要的 。	we need some kind of error redundancy to make sure that what we're successful is what we want .
因此 , 我要向各位展示一些我和我的同事正在進行的要實現這種自我組裝的未來的專案 。	so i'm going to show you a few of the projects that my colleagues and i are working on to make this selfassembly possible future project .
頭兩個專案是macrobot和decibot 。	the first two projects are macrobot and decibot .
這些專案都是大規模可重構機器人8英尺 , 12英尺長的蛋白質 。	these projects are eight feet of reframable robots , 12 feet long proteins .
它們嵌入機電裝置 , 感測器 。	they're embedded in a machine , a sensor .
你需要把想要摺疊的方式解碼成 , 解碼成一系列角度負120度 , 負120度 , 0度 , 0度 , 120度 , 負120度 , 這類的東西 ; 一系列角度 , 或轉向 , 可以用電線把這個次序傳過去 。	you have to decode the way you want to fold in a series of 120 degrees , minus 120 degrees angles , zero , 0 , 120 degrees , minus 120 degrees , that kind of thing ; a series of angles , or diversions , that sort of thing can be passed through this sequence with wires .
每個單元獲取自己的訊息比如負120.它進行旋轉 , 檢查是否旋轉到位然後把序列傳給它的鄰居 。	each unit gets its own message , like minus 120 . it rotates , checks for whether or not it spins to its neighbors .
有許多傑出的科學家 , 工程師 , 設計師為這個專案工作 。	there are brilliant scientists , engineers , designers working on this project .
我認為這一專案真的揭示出:這真的可擴充套件麼 ?	and i think this project really reveals: is it really scalable ?
我是說 , 花費數千美元許多人時來製造這個八英尺的機器人 。	i mean , it costs thousands of dollars to build this eightfoot robot over a lot of people .
我們真的能擴大它麼 ? 我們真的能在每個部分中都嵌入機器人麼 ?	can we really expand that ? can we actually embed robots within each part ?
下一個問題是看看被動性 , 或被動地嘗試讓重組具有可程式設計性 。	the next question is looking at passive nature , or passively attempting to make recombinations programmable .
但它更進了一步 , 它嘗試進行實際計算 。	but it went further , and it tried to do actual computation .
基本上嵌入了多數計算的基礎構建模組 , 數字邏輯閘 , 直接進入各個部分 。	it's basically embedded in most computational building modules , the digital gates directly into each other .
這是與非門 。	this is a nationstate .
每個要用於計算的門上都有一個四面體 , 有兩個輸入四面體 。	each door of the calculations has a tetrahedron that has two inputs in it .
其中一個是來自使用者的輸入 , 就像你在構建磚塊 。	one of them is the input from the user , just like you're building bricks .
另一個是來之前前放好的一塊磚的輸入 。	the other is the input of a brick that came before .
接著它會給出三維空間的輸出 。	and then it will give the threedimensional output .
這意味著使用者以他們想要的方式堆砌磚塊 。	that means users build bricks in the way they want .
它依據之前所做的和你的指令進行計算 。	it computes based on what it was done and what your instructions have done .
現在它開始在三維空間內移動上或者下 。	now it starts moving up or down in three dimensions .
看左面 , [1 , 1]的輸入等於0輸出 , 表示向下 。	look at the left , [1 , 1] input equals 0 output , and that means down .
在右邊 , [0 , 0]的輸入是1輸出 , 表示向上 。	on the right , [0 , zero] input is a 1 output , upwards .
因此這真正的的意味是我們的結構中現在包含了我們想要構建的藍圖 。	so that really means that our structure now contains the blueprints that we want to build .
因此關於想要構建的事物的資訊已經全部嵌入其中 。	so the information about the things that want to be constructed has embedded them all .
這意味著我們有了某種形式的自我複製 。	that means we have some form of selfreplication .
對這種情況 , 我稱之為自我導向複製 , 因為你的結構中包含了精確的藍圖 。	in this case , i call this selfdirecting replication , because the exact blueprint in your structures .
如果遇到錯誤 , 你可以替換一個部分 。	if you have a error , you can replace a part .
所有的本地資訊都嵌入其中 , 告訴你如何修復它 。	so all of this local information is embedded in telling you how you can repair it .
因此你有個可以攀爬的東西 , 能讀出它並一個一個的輸出 。	so you have something that can climb , read out it and an output .
它是直接嵌入的 ; 沒有外部指令輸入 。	it's directly embedded ; it has no external instructions .
我要展示的最後一個專案名為偏心鏈條 , 它可能是我們現在看到的被動自我裝配系統中最令人激動的例子 。	the last project i'm going to show is called biased chain , and it's probably the most exciting example we're looking at right now in the passive selfassembly system .
它具有可重構性和可程式設計性使它成了為了一個完全地被動系統 。	it has reorganism and programmability that makes it a completely passive system .
基本上就是你有了一連串的元素 。	it's basically a series of elements that you have .
每個元素都是完全相同的 , 且它們是偏心的 。	each element is completely identical , and they're biased .
每個鏈條 , 或每個元素想要向右轉或是向左轉 。	each chain , or every element , wants to turn right or left .
如果你要裝配鏈條 , 需要為它程式設計 。	if you want the chain link , you need to program it .
要告訴每個單元是要左轉還是右轉 。	to tell each component is to turn the left or the right .
當你搖動這個鏈條時 , 它就摺疊起來程式設計你所為它編碼的任何結構因此這種情況下 , 一個螺旋體 , 火這種情況 , 兩個相連的立方體 。	when you shake the chain , it folds up and codes whatever structure you encode for , so in this case , a spiral , fire , two connected cubes .
基本上你可以在三維空間內程式設計或是一維、二維這鏈條是完全被動的 。	you can basically program it in three dimensions , or on one dimension , and the chain of two dimensions is completely passive .
這向我們預示了怎樣的未來呢 ?	what kind of future does that tell us ?
我認為這告訴我們這些在我們的身體結構、我們的建築和機器中這種自我裝配、自我複製和自我修復的可能性 。	and i think this tells us the possibilities for selfassembly and selfreplication and selfrepair in our bodies , our architecture and our machines .
在這些部分中有新的可程式設計性 。	there's new programmability in these parts .
從中你能獲得計算的新可能性 。	you've got new possibilities for calculating .
我們將有空間計算 。	we'll have spatial computing .
想象一下我們的建築、橋樑、機器 , 所有的磚塊都能進行實際計算 。	imagine our buildings , our bridges , our machines , all the bricks are capable of actually calculating .
多麼令人驚奇的平行計算和分散式計算能力和新的設計可能性啊 。	what an amazing possibility of parallel computing and distributed computing and new design .
這是項令人激動的潛力 。	it's an exciting potential .
我認為這些我向各位展示的專案僅僅是邁向未來的一小步 , 如果我們為一個新的自我組裝的世界實現了這些新技術的話 。	i think these projects that i'm showing you are just a tiny step towards the future , if we implement these new technologies as a world of selfassembly .
我們已踏上過月球 , 我們已測繪了大陸 , 我們甚至已去過海底最深處--兩次 。 還剩下什麼值得我們的下一代去探索 ? 生物學家和內森•沃爾夫提出了這樣的答案:幾乎所有事物 。 " 我們可以從那小到看不見的世界開始 " , 他說 。	we've been on the moon , we've mapped the continent , we've even been to the bottom twice . what's left with our children ? biologist and nathan wolf gives an answer like this: almost everything , " we can start with that little to see , " he said .
biodiversity , exploration , microbiology , science	sodiversity , idiological nursery , biology .
內森•沃爾夫:還有什麼值得探索 ?	nathan wolf: what else is it worth exploring ?
最近我去了威斯康星州的伯洛伊特市 。	i recently went to beloit , wisconsin .
我去那裡是為了紀念一名20世紀的探險家 , 羅伊•查普曼•安德魯斯 。	i went there to honor a 20thcentury explorer , roy chapman andrews .
當他在美國自然歷史博物館的時候 , 安德魯斯領導了一系列對未知領域的探險 , 比如說在這裡的戈壁灘 。	when he was in the american museum of natural history , andrews led a series of expeditions to the unknown , such as the kobe beach here .
他是個了不起的人物 。	he was a fantastic man .
他後來據說是印第安娜瓊斯角色的原型 。	he reported it was the prototype of the indiana jones character .
當我在威斯康星州的伯洛伊特市的時候 , 我給一群中學學生上了一堂公開課 。	when i was in beloitt , wisconsin , i gave a bunch of middle school students an open course .
我現在想告訴你們 , 如果真的有什麼比在ted做演講還難的話 , 那就是嘗試保持他們的注意力一群上千個12歲的孩子 , 並保持45分鐘 。	and i want to tell you right now , if anything is even more difficult than giving a talk at ted , it's trying to pay attention to a bunch of thousands of 12yearolds for 45 minutes .
在我講完之後 , 他們問了很多問題 , 但有一個讓我自始至終難以忘記 。	after i finished my talk , they asked a lot of questions , but there was one that i'll never forget .
有個小女孩站起來 , 問了一個問題: " 我們該去哪裡探索呢 ? "	and this little girl stood up and she asked the question , " where are we going to explore ? "
我想我們中的絕大多數有種觀念 , 那就是 , 地球上的大探索時代已經結束 , 我們的下一代人應該去外太空或者海洋最深處從而去尋找值得探索的東西 。	i think most of us have the concept that the big age of exploration on earth is over , that our children should go to outer space or the deepest of the oceans to find something worth exploring .
但真的是這樣嗎 ?	but is that really the case ?
真的沒有重要的地方留給我們探索了嗎 ? 整個地球上都沒有 ?	isn't it really important to leave us with an exploration , an entire planet with nowhere ?
這讓我回憶起我最喜歡的生物領域的探險家之一 。	this reminds me of one of my favorite explorers in the biological realm .
他是位未知世界的探索家 , 馬丁努斯•威廉•拜耶林克 。	he was an explorer of the unknown world , martinus william bayeric .
拜葉林克當初想找出引起菸草花葉病的原因 。	byeye yellow identified why it caused tobacco leaf disease .
他提取了受過感染的菸草汁液 , 然後讓這些汁液經過一層比一層更細的過濾 。	he extracted the infected tobacco sap , and then he released it through a thinner filter than a layer of other filters .
他得出一個結論 , 剩下的裡面一定有什麼東西它們比那時最小的已知的生命形態--細菌 , 還要小 。	and he came to the conclusion that there must be something inside of it that was smaller than the smallest known lifestyle bacteria , smaller .
他給這個神秘的東西起了個名字	he gives this mysterious thing a name .
叫它們 , 病毒在拉丁文裡是 " 毒藥 " 的意思 。	call them the virus means " poison " in latin .
在發現病毒之後 , 拜耶林克為我們打開了一個全新的世界 。	after discovering the virus , bayerinek opened up a whole new world for us .
我們現在知道病毒構成我們星球上絕大部分的遺傳資訊超過所有其他生命的遺傳資訊的總和 。	we now know that viruses make up most of the genetic information on our planet more than the sum of all other lifeforms on all of our planet .
而且顯然已經出現了無數有關病毒的切實應用在這個世界上--像天花的根除 , 子宮癌的疫苗的降臨--我們現在知道它大部分是由乳頭瘤病毒引起的 。	and it's obviously been applied to countless cut virus applications in the world like the root of smallpox eradication , the flu vaccine in cervical cancer which we now know is mostly caused by sarcoma .
而且拜耶林克的發現可不是500年前的事情 。	and what bayeringk discovered was not 500 years ago .
拜耶林克發現病毒這件事也就發生於100多年前 。	this happened more than 100 years ago by bayerine found out about the virus .
也就是說當汽車都已經出現在世的時候 , 我們還不知道這種構成了我們星球上大部分的遺傳資訊的生物 。	so what that means is that when cars are dead , we don't yet know that's what makes most of the genetic information on our planet .
我們現在有些很了不起的工具來幫助我們探索未知世界 , 像基因深度測序 , 可以讓我們不只是停留在表面來看自某個特定物種的獨立基因組 , 而是研究整個基因組--我們身體裡面和周邊無處不在的微生物群落 , 並且記錄下這些物種的遺傳資訊 。	we now have some incredible tools to help us explore the unknown world , like a genetic depth , that allow us not just to pause on the surface to see individual genomes from a particular species , but to study the entire genome the microbial community that we're all in and around to record the genetic information of these species .
我們可以應用這些技術來研究從土壤到皮膚和它們中間的一切 。	we can use these technologies to study everything from soil to skin and everything in between .
在我所在的機構裡面 , 我們現在經常這麼做 , 來尋找暴發的原因 , 那些我們還不清楚的原因.	in my institution , we now do this all the time , looking for causes of abuse , for reasons we don't know .
稍微給你們講下這是怎麼做的 , 想象下從你們每個人那裡取一個鼻腔分泌物標本	and just to give you a snapshot of how it works . here's an imaginary icon of where each of you is taking a nasal secretary label
像這種事是我們經常做的 , 為了尋找呼吸道病毒 , 像流行性感冒病毒 。	these are the kinds of things that we often do to search for respiratory viruses , like influenza .
我們首先看到的是海量的遺傳資訊 。	the first thing we saw was the volume of genetic information .
如果我們開始仔細看看這些遺傳資訊 , 我們會看到一些常見的資訊當然了 , 有很多人類的遺傳資訊 , 但也有很多細菌和病毒的資訊 , 大部分是你鼻子裡面完全無害的東西 。	if we start to look at these genetic information , we see some common information , and of course there's a lot of human inheritance , but there's also a lot of bacteria and virus data that's mostly harmless within your nose .
但我們也會看到一些非常非常讓人吃驚的東西 。	but we also see some very , very surprising things .
當我們開始研究這些資訊 , 我們會發現你鼻子裡面20%的遺傳資訊跟我們所見過的東西--任何植物 , 動物 , 真菌或者細菌 , 都對不上號 。	when we start to study this information , we find that 20 percent of the genetic information in your nose is inherited to anything we've seen any plant , animals , fungi , or bacteria , that's irrelevant .
我們基本上對這些一無所知 。	we basically don't know anything about it .
我們這裡的一小部分研究這些資料的人們 , 稱呼這些資訊為生物暗物質 。	a small portion of us here are calling this information biological dark matter .
我們知道以前從未見過這些生物暗物質 ; 這似乎可以被稱之為我們自己遺傳資訊裡的未知大陸 。	we know that we've never seen one of these biological dark matters ; it seems to be called the unknown continent of our own inherited information .
而且數量非常之多 。	and there's a lot of them .
如果你認為你鼻子裡面20%的遺傳資訊有很多生物暗物質 , 那當我們看你內臟的時候 , 那有將近40%到50%的生物暗物質 。	if you think 20 percent of the genetic information in your nose has lots of biological dark matter , then when we look at your gut , there's almost 40 to 50 percent biological dark matter .
即使在相對無菌的血液裡 , 也有1%到2%的資訊是暗物質--無法被歸類 , 無法被判別類別 , 跟我們所見過的東西都不同 。	even in the relatively sterile blood , there's one to two percent of the information that's dark matter can't be categorized , can't be categorized , can't be categorized , can't be categorized , can't be categorized .
開始我們以為這是人為的東西 。	at first , we thought it was a human thing .
這些基因深度測序工具相當比較新 。	these genetic instruments are quite new .
但當它們變得越來越來精確 , 我們認為這些資訊是一種新的生命 , 或者至少某一部分是種生命 。	but as they become more and more precise , we think that this information is a new form of life , or at least a part of it is a form of life .
即使這些關於解釋生物暗物質的存在的假設還處於嬰兒期 , 一個讓人非常非常激動的可能性存在著:那就是藏在這個生命裡面 , 在這些遺傳資訊裡 , 有一種沒有被識別的生命的標識 。	even these assumptions about the presence of biological dark matter are in infancy , a very , very exciting possibility exists in our infancy: that's hidden within this life , and in those genetic information , there's a unidentified identification of life .
當我們探索這些一串串a/t/c/g嘌呤的時候 , 我們也許會發現全新的生命 , 就像拜耶林克 , 從根本上改變我們對生物學特性的理解 。	when we explore these series of a/c/g purines , we may find new life , like bayelink , that fundamentally changes our understanding of biology .
這也許會讓我識別出困擾我們的某種癌症的原因 , 或者識別出我們不熟悉的疾病暴發的根源 , 或者創造出一種分子生物學的新工具 。	this may make me identify the cause of a cancer , or identify the source of a familiar disease atrocities , or create a new tool in molecular biology .
我很高興的宣佈 , 和我的斯坦福、加州理工和舊金山加利福尼亞大學的同事們一起 , 我們正在開始開始一個新的行動去探索生物暗物質來尋找新生命的存在 。	i'm pleased to announce that with my stanford and caltech and my colleagues at the university of california at san francisco , we're starting a new movement to explore the existence of biological dark matter .
100多年前 , 人們還不知道病毒的存在 , 這些包含我們星球上大部分遺傳資訊的生命形態 。	more than 100 years ago , people didn't know that the virus existed , these forms of life that contain most of the genetic information on our planet .

未知的事物在我們身邊無處不在它們只是在等待人類的探索 。	the unknowns are all around us , they're just waiting for human exploration .

物體 , 不管他們彼此多麼相異 , 卻仍然能夠表現同樣的數學和因果結構 , 而且隨著時間增長表現得越來越多 。	objects , no matter how different they are , can still behave the same mathematical and causal structure as they grow longer in time .

那麼太陽系--我們的環境 , 以我們的形式--是如何獲取這樣一個與宇宙其他部分的特殊關係的呢 ?	solar system how do our environment , in our form , get this special relationship to the rest of the universe ?
stephenhawking觀點中其中一個正確面--我的意思是 , 這是正確的 , 但是著重點是錯的 。 其中一個正確面是它並沒有倚賴任何特殊的物理學 。 沒有特殊的放寬 , 沒有奇蹟發生 。 它的發生只依賴於我們現在富有的三種東西 。	one of the accurate aspects of stephen hawking's perspective i mean , this is true , but the point is that it doesn't rely on any particular physics . there's no special bandwidth , no miracles .
其中一個是物質 , 因為知識的增長是一種資訊處理的形式 。 資訊處理需要計算 , 計算需要電腦--現有的知識下不可能不需要物質來製造電腦 。	one of them is substance , because knowledge grows is a form of information processing that requires calculation , calculation it doesn't really need the material to make a computer .
我們還需要能量來製造電腦 , 最重要的是 , 要使得用來記錄我們所發現知識的媒介工作 。	we also need energy to make a computer , and most importantly , to make the media that we have discovered .

我們的環境中充滿了證據 。	our environment is full of evidence .
但是我們常常忽略了測試--比如 , 牛頓的地球引力定律--大約是在300年前提出的 。	but we tend to ignore the tests so for example , newton's law of gravitational laws of gravity about 300 years ago .
但是我們習以為常的證據 , 從數十億年前就在地球上的每個角落裡不斷墜落 , 也會在接下來的數十億年裡繼續墜落 。 其他科學也同樣如此 。	but the evidence that we're used to , we've fallen in every corner of the globe from billions of years ago , and we're going to continue to fall for billions of years .
