我們所在的地方充滿了證據 , 還有物質和能量 。	we are located with evidence and also with matter and energy .
而在星系間的空間中 , 這三個創造開放式知識的前提條件存在的可能性極端之小 。	and in intergalactic space , these three premises for the openended creation of knowledge are incredibly small .
正如我所說 , 那裡空無一物 , 寒冷 , 黑暗 。 抑或不是如此 ?	as i say , there's nothing , it's cold , it's dark , it's not like that .
事實上 , 這只是另外一個狹隘的誤解 。	in fact , it's just another narrow misconception .
假想在星系間空間有一個立方體存在 , 與我們的房屋般大小 , 太陽系 。 以我們的標準來看 , 這個立方體非常空 , 但是它事實上仍然包含著超過百萬噸的物質 。	imagine a cube that exists in intergalactic space the size of our house , the solar system , on our standards , the cube is very empty , but it still contains over a million tons of material .
一百萬噸足夠建造一個 , 比方說 , 自給自足的空間站 , 在這個空間站內聚居著一群科學家 , 他們致力於不斷創造開放式的知識 , 等等 。	one million tons is enough to build , let's say , a selfsufficient space station where a group of scientists sitting on this space , engaging in an openended creation of knowledge , and so on .
然而 , 現在的科技甚至連從星系間空間收集氫氣和將其轉化成別的元素等都遠不能做到 。	however , today's technologies even gather hydrogen from intergalactic space and convert it into other elements and so forth .
但問題是 , 在一個可理解的宇宙中 , 如果某事是物理定律所允許的 , 那麼在我們知道如何運作的情況下 , 什麼會妨礙我們去實踐它呢 ?	but the question is , in a comprehensible universe , if something is allowed by the laws of physics , then what might prevent us from doing it under the conditions that we know how ?
換句話說 , 這是一個關於知識的問題 , 而不是關於資源 。	in other words , it's a matter of knowledge , not resources .
同樣 , 如果我們可以做到的話 , 那麼我們將自動獲得能源供給 , 因為這裡的變化將是核反應堆--證據 ?	and similarly , if we can do that , then we'll automatically have an energy supply , because what's going to happen here is a nuclear reaction , evidence ?
還是一樣 , 對人類的感官來說那裡漆黑一片 。 但是你所需要做的是拿起一個望遠鏡 , 甚至是今天的技術設計 , 往外看去 , 你會看到我們從這兒看到的同樣的星系 。	again , dark out there for human senses , but all you have to do is pick up a telescope , even today's technology , and look out , and you'll see the same galaxy that we're seeing from here .
如果你有一個更強大的望遠鏡 , 你將能看到恆星和行星 。	if you have a more powerful telescope , you'll see stars and planets .
在那些星系裡 , 你可以進行天體物理學研究 , 瞭解物理定律 。	in those galaxies , you can perform astrophysics study to understand the laws of physics .
在你所處的位置 , 你可以製造粒子加速器 , 研究初級粒子物理學 , 化學等 。	where you sit , you can build particle accelerators , you study primary particle physics , chemistry , etc .
也許最難做的科學研究是生物學實地考察 , 因為需要花費數百萬年才能往返最近的有生命的星球 。	perhaps the hardest scientific research is the field of biology , because it takes millions of years to travel back to the nearest living planet .
但是我必須告訴你--對不起 , richard--但是我從來都不是那麼喜歡生物學實地考察 , 我想我們可以每數百萬年才進行一次 。	but i have to tell you i'm sorry richard but i never really liked the field of biology , and i think we can do it every million years .
因此事實上 , 星系間空間並不具備創造開放式知識的前提條件 。 任何一個這樣的立方體 , 在宇宙中任何地方 , 都可以成為跟我們一樣的中心 , 如果履行這一計劃的知識確實存在的話 。	so , in fact , intergalactic space does not have the prerequisite for the openended creation of knowledge , and any cube like this could be the same hub that we have in the universe , if the knowledge of the project exists .
因此我們並不是唯一熱情好客的地方 。	so we're not the only place we're passionate about it .
如果星系間空間可以創造出一串開放式的解說 , 那麼幾乎其它所有的環境都是可以的 。 地球也一樣 。 被汙染的地球也是一樣 。	if intergalactic space creates an openended stream of explanations , then pretty much every other environment is fine , so does the earth .
而限制性因素 , 這裡和那裡 , 不是資源 , 因為資源很充沛 , 而是知識 , 非常匱乏 。	and the limiting factor , here and there , is not resources , because resources are enormous , but knowledge , are scarce .
這樣一個知識型的宇宙觀也許--我認為應該--讓我們感覺非常不平凡 。 但同時也讓我們感覺到自己的脆弱 , 因為這也意味著如果沒有那些必需的具體的知識來幫助我們應對宇宙中源源不斷地挑戰 , 我們將無法生存 。	this cosmic observation of knowledge may and i think it should make us feel very extraordinary , but it also makes us feel vulnerable , because it means that without those necessary knowledge to help us respond to constantly challenging the source of the universe , we will not survive
僅僅是幾光年外的一個超新星爆炸 , 我們都將必死無疑 。	it's just a supernova explosion a few lightyears away , and we're all going to be dead .
martinrees最近剛寫了一本關於我們人類對於所有事物的脆弱性的書 , 從天體物理學 , 到科學實驗事故 , 還有最重要的擁有大規模殺傷性武器的恐怖主義 。	martin inrees has recently written a book about our vulnerability to all things , from astrophysics to the scientific experimental crash , and most importantly , terrorism with weapons of mass destruction .
他認為人類文明只有50%的機率可以存活過這個世紀 。	he believed that civilization had only a 50 percent chance of surviving this century .
我想他晚些時候會在這個會上給大家講述 。	i think he'll tell you later about this conference .
但是我認為這一問題並不適合用機率來描述 。	but i don't think that's the right question for probability .
但是我同意他就此的看法 。 我們可以生存下去 , 我們也可能不會存續 。	but i agree with him , and we can survive , and we may not survive .
但是這並不取決於機率 , 而是我們是否可以及時創造出相關的知識 。	but it doesn't depend on probability , it's whether we can create relevant knowledge in time .
這種危險肯定不是前所未有的 。 物種一直都在滅絕 。	this danger is definitely not unprecedented . species continue to go extinct .
文明也會終止 。 絕大多數存在過的物種和文明都以成歷史 。	civilizations end . the vast majority of species and civilizations live in history .
如果我們想成為例外的話 , 邏輯上來看我們唯一的希望是利用將我們這個種群和文明與其他物種區別開的這個特徵 , 與其他一切都區別開的這個特徵 。 也就是 , 我們與物理定律得特殊關係 。 我們創造新的解釋和知識的能力--成為存在的中心 。	if we want to be the exception , logically , our only hope is to use the trait that distinguishes our species and civilization from all other species , and that is , we have a special relationship with the laws of physics , and our ability to create new explanations and new knowledge to be the hub of existence .
讓我將此運用到當前的一個論戰中 , 不是因為我想提議任何特定的解決方法 , 而只是用來闡明我所要講述的一些事 。	and let me use this to a current argument , not because i want to propose any particular solution , but just to illustrate some of the things i'm going to talk about .
這個論戰就是全球暖化 。	this controversy is global warming .
我是一個物理學家 , 但我並不是此領域的物理學家 。 就全球暖化來說 , 我只是個門外漢 。 對一個門外漢來說理智的做法是嚴肅對待權威的科學理論 。 而根據這一理論 , 已經太晚了 , 災難在所難免 。	i'm a physicist , but i'm not the physicist in this field , but as a global warming external , i'm just a serious externality to an outsider , and according to this theory , disaster strikes .
因為 , 如果我們目前最好的選擇是阻止二氧化碳排放的話 , 例如透過東京議定書之類的 , 限制經濟活動 , 以及花費千億美元等巨大的代價 , 那麼不管如何衡量 , 這就已經是一個災難了 。	because if our current best option is to block co2 emissions , for example , tokyo protocols and so on , restrict economic activity and the cost of hundreds of billions of dollars , then this is a disaster , no matter how we measure it .
倡議的行動甚至都不是為解決問題 , 而只是稍微推遲災難的到來 。 因此災難在所難免 , 一切都已晚 , 或在所有人意識到這個危險之前就已經太晚了 。	the actions of advocacy are not even about solving the problem , but slightly pushing the disaster , and so the disaster is too late , or it's too late for anyone to even recognize this danger .
上世紀70年代的時候也許就已經太晚了 , 那時候最先進的科學理論告訴我們工業排放將促成一個新的冰河世紀 , 數十億的人類將從此滅亡 。	it was probably too late in the 1970s , when the most advanced scientific theory told us that industrial emissions were about to contribute to a new ice age , that billions of people were going to die from it .
這一教訓對我來說清晰可見 , 我不明白為什麼它沒有傳達至公眾辯論 。	and the lesson for me is clear , and i don't know why it doesn't communicate to public debate .
事實是我們不可能永遠知道 。 當我們知道有一個災難將要降臨 , 應對這個災難的成本要比災難本身小 , 那麼就真的沒有什麼好爭論的 。	the fact that we can't always know , when we know that there's a disaster that's coming to an end that has to be smaller than the disaster itself , there's really no good argument about it .
但是沒有任何預防措施 , 或者預防原則可以幫助我們避免我們還沒有預測到的問題 。	but no precautions , no precautionary principle can help us avoid problems we haven't anticipated yet .
因此我們需要準備好去解決問題 , 而不僅僅是避免問題 。	so we need to be ready to solve the problem , not just avoid the problem .
一盎司的預防等於一盎司的解決 , 這是事實 , 但是這只是在我們知道預防什麼的情況下 。	an ounce of prevention equals an ounce of solving , which is true , but it's only in case we know what prevention is .
如果你的鼻子被打了一拳 , 醫學不會教你如何閃躲拳頭 。	if you're punched in your nose , medicine does not teach you how to get out of your fists .
如果醫學不再研究治病的方法 , 而是僅僅研究預防 , 那麼它將幾乎一事無成 。	if medicine stops studying the disease , but only studying prevention , then it's almost impossible .
目前整個世界都在不計成本地忙著計劃來促成氣體排放量的減少 。	the world's currently engaged in terms of planning to promote reduction in gas emissions .
而它應該趕緊計劃如何降低溫度 , 以及計劃如何在溫度升高之後如何生存 。 不是不計成本 , 而是有效地、廉價的計劃 。 而這樣的一些計劃已經存在了 , 比如在太空中放置大批鏡子來將太陽光反射出去 , 以及刺激海洋生物消費更多的二氧化碳 。	and it should be planning to reduce the temperature and plan how to survive at the temperature rising , not in terms of cost , but inexpensively and inexpensive planning , and in some cases already exist , such as installing a bunch of mirrors in space to reflect sunlight and stimulate more carbon dioxide .
而目前 , 這些都只是邊緣研究 。	now , these are just the marginal research .
人類在應對這個問題或者廣義上來說這些問題的時候 , 它們起不到核心作用 。	when it comes to tackling this problem or broadly speaking , they don't have a core effect .
對於我們並未知覺的問題 , 糾錯的能力--不是無限期的躲過期發生的絕對好運--是我們唯一的希望 , 不僅僅是為解決問題 , 而是為生存 。	the capacity for the unknown , the ability to get things wrong is not the absolute good luck to happen indefinitely in the hiding period it's our only hope , not just for the problem , but for survival .
我們應該拿起兩塊石碑 , 在上邊刻上銘文 。	we should pick up two stone monuments and carve on the top .
其中一塊刻上 " 問題是可以解決的 " 。	on one of them , carve: " problems are soluble . "
另外一塊刻上 " 問題是不可避免的 " 。	the other one carves on: " the problem is inevitable . "
被困在不健全的制度下 , 一個國家怎麼可能脫貧呢 ? 經濟學家paulromer提出全新見解: " 特別市 " , 由多國聯合政府管理的、城市規模的管理區域 。	trapped in the unhealthy system , how could a nation get out of poverty , and the economist paul romer asks new insights: " special market , " managed by multinational united nations , urbanscale areas .
business , culture , economics , globalissues , politics	it's good of us , it's good of us , it's good of us .
paulromer的全新見解:特別市	paul romer's new insight: special markets .
請看這張圖片 。	take a look at this picture .
它帶給我們一個極具吸引力的謎 。	it gives us an attractive puzzle .
這些非洲學生在做功課在首都機場的街燈下因為他們家裡沒有電 。	these african students are doing their homework under the streets of the airport because they don't have electricity in their homes .
我還沒見過這幾個學生本人但我見過像他們一樣的學生 。	i haven't seen these students yet , but i've seen students like them .
拿那個穿綠襯衫的學生做例子 ,	take the student in the green shirt .
假設他的名字叫做nelson 。	let's say his name is nelson .
我猜他肯定有個手機	i guess he had a phone .
有趣的是 ,	and here's the funny thing .
為什麼nelson有機會享用像手機這樣的前沿科技成果但卻不能在家用上電力 ? 人們早在100年前就已經發明瞭這一科技啊 ?	why is it that nelson had the opportunity to enjoy a frontline technological outcome like our phones , but couldn't use it at home , where people had invented this technology 100 years earlier ?
答案是 " 制度 " 。	the answer is institutions .
不健全的制度會妨礙這種雙贏節決辦法的產生人們在一定的制度之下就不會將科技帶給像nelson這樣的人	the robust institutions impede the creation of this winwin solution , and people wouldn't bring technology to people like nelson under certain rules .
什麼樣的制度呢 ?	what kind of rules ?
這個國家的電力公司需要遵守一條制度這個制度要求它在政府補貼的條件下從使用者收取極其低價電費事實上 , 電費便宜到另電力公司虧損的地步	the power company in this nation needs to follow a system that demands it to charge extremes from the government's subsidy , and in fact , the electricity bill is cheaper to add in terms of losses to the different companies .
所以 , 電力公司既沒有資源 , 也沒有動機去給使用者接通電源	so the power company has no resources , no motivation for the user .
總統想要改變這個局面	the president wanted to change that .
他已經覺察到更換體制是具可能性的 。 能讓商家盈利的體制才能使有動機爭取更多使用者	he's been aware that replacement systems is possible , and it's possible for merchants to be profitable so that they can motivate more users .
賣nelson的手機的那個廠家也正式在制度下經營著	the manufacturer selling nelson's phones also formally run in the system .
總統已經領會到制度執行良好	the president has come to recognition of good rules .
所以他嘗試著改變現行的電價制度但來自商人以及消費者的反對的聲音四起他們想保留現行的補貼電費制度	so he attempted to reverse the prices of current electricity , but came from traders and consumers , and went on and off , and they wanted to retain the subsidy .
總統無能為力 , 只能任由現行制度阻止雙贏局面產生 , 任由它妨礙改善國家	the president can't do anything , but can stop the winwin situation from happening in the present institutions and improve the country .
因此 , nelson也只能在街燈下學習	so nelson can only study under the streetlights .
真正具有挑戰性的是嘗試尋找改變制度的辦法	what is really challenging is trying to find a way to change rules .
我們可不可以發展 " 改變制度 " 的制度呢 ?	can we develop the rules for changing rules ?
我想說 , 我們可以把抽象化為實際或者說 , 如果我們給予人民更多選擇給予領導者更多選擇 , 領導者在很多國家也是人民麼	i mean , we can turn abstract into a practical reality , or if we give people more choices , more choices to leaders , and more leaders , in many countries , are also people .
但 , 兩者間的對立還是有必要解釋的	but the polarity of the opposition is necessary .
因為你想給予領袖的自由是像那種你給予總統提高電價一樣的自由剝奪人民在這個經濟體系中的需求自由	because the freedom you're giving leaders is like the freedom you're giving the president to raise the price of electricity , the freedom of the people in the economy .
希望可以繼續享用補貼電價的自由	we hope to continue to enjoy the freedom of subsidized prices .
所以如果你只選取一方 , 或另一方你將面臨矛盾或摩擦	so if you just choose one side , or the other , you're going to face contradictions or friction .
但如果我們相辦法同時給兩者自由那麼就會產生能使我們擺脫困境的制度	but if we can do this together , if we give both , then we can have institutions that escape our dilemma .
nelson現在還可以享用網際網路	nelson can also use the internet now .

特別注意一下亞洲	ok , notice the asia .

你不會驚訝北朝鮮的制度將人民陷於黑暗	you wouldn't be surprised that north korea's institutions are catching people in the dark .
重要的是要承認南北朝鮮曾有一模一樣的制度不論法律上還是政策上而且在深層理解上準則 , 文化 , 價值 , 信仰	it's important to recognize that north korea had exactly the same set of rules , regardless of law , policies , deep understanding of principles , cultures , values , faiths .
南北分隔時 , 南北朝鮮做出了引領它們走向不同道路的選擇由不同的制度而產生	in the northern part , southern north korea led the choice to different roads , led by different institutions .
因而我們可以改變 , 我們 , 人類 , 可以改變制度人際交往與相處的制度使之變得更好 , 或更壞	so we can change , we , humans , can change the institutions of intercourse and adaptations to make them better or worse .
現在來看看另外一個地區 , 加勒比海域	let's look at another region , the caribbean .
放大海地在這兒	here we see the magnification of haiti .
海地也在黑暗中和鄰國多明尼加共和國相比同樣的人口總數	haiti is also in the dark with neighboring countries , the dominican republic , compared to the same population .
但這兩個國家和波多黎各比 , 也處於黑暗中波多黎各人口總數大概是海地或多米尼亞共和國的一半左右	but these two countries compared to puerto rico , also in dark puerto rico , which is about half the population of haiti and dominicans .

因此如果我們想要建立良好政策的環境我們不能總是破壞	so if we want to create environments of good policy , we can't always destroy it .

中國最明亮的地域你可以在輪廓的邊際看到是香港	the brightest terrain in china , you can see it on the edge of the stockpile , is hong kong .
香港其實是中國很小的一塊地方在二十世紀的絕大部分時期都在非常不同的體制下治理著與大陸其它地方都不同體制是從當時有效的市場經濟複製出來的並由英國治理	hong kong was actually a small area in china , and in the vast majority of the 20th century , the governing of a very different system was unlike the rest of the continent , which was replicated from a very effective market economy and governed by britain .

這些的成功引起共識帶領整個經濟體制走向市場經濟	these successes have led to consensus , and the whole economy is headed towards the market economy .

另一方面 , 一下子改變全國的體制又太大了	on the other hand , the system was too big to change the country .

並且足夠大大到我們能得到應有的當百萬人在新體制治理下應有的效應	and it's big enough that we get the effects that we deserve for the millions of people in new institutions .

約在十年前我們對基因組學發展的設想是到今年年底的時候我們或許能完成3到5個基因組的測序而事實上已經完成了數百個	about a decade ago , our assumptions about genomics were that by the end of this year , we might have sequenced three to five genomes , and actually hundreds of them .
我們剛剛從戈登-貝蒂•摩爾基金會獲得一筆資助作為環境有機體專案的副專案我們將在今年完成130個基因組的測序	we've just gotten a grant from gordon betty moore foundation , and we're going to sequence 130 genomes this year as an environmental organism .
閱讀遺傳編碼的速率已然改變	the rate of reading genetic code has changed .

大多數人沒有意識到這些肉眼看不到的生物微生物構成了地球約一半的生物量而所有的動物加起來也才佔地球生物量的千分之一	most people don't realize that the microbes invisible to our naked eyes make up about half the biomass of our planet , and that all animals combined make up onethousandth of our planet's biomass .
跑到海邊喝上一口海水或許不是牛津人經常做的事但請記住每一毫升的海水裡有大約一百萬個的細菌其中的病毒更是以千萬計	go to the beach and have a bite of seawater maybe not by oxford , but keep in mind that each milliliter of seawater has about a million bacteria , and the virus involves tens of millions .
兩年前只有不到五千種的微生物被鑑定歸類於是我們決定做些這方面的事情	less than 5 , 000 microbes were identified two years ago , and we decided to do something about it .
我們啟動了巫師二號考察和其他大型的海洋考察活動一樣我們嘗試每200英里採一次樣	we started the shaman ii expedition , and we did the same with other major oceanographic expeditions , and we tried it every 200 miles .
考察伊始 , 我們在百慕大進行了測試專案然後前往哈利法克斯接著到美國東海岸加勒比海、巴拿馬運河穿過加拉帕哥斯群島 , 然後橫跨太平洋現在我們正在穿越印度洋的過程中	inspector , we conducted a pilot program in bermuda , and went to halifax and went to the east coast of caribbean , the panama canal , through the galapagos , and then across the pacific , and now we're in the process of crossing the indian ocean .
工作很艱難 , 我們乘著一艘帆船某種程度上我們想透過它激起年輕人投身科學的興趣	it's hard work , we're taking a sailing boat and we're kind of interested in it by sparking young people into science .
實驗其實非常簡單	and the experiment was very simple .
採集海水 , 過濾用不同的過濾器採集不同大小的生物然後把它們的dna帶回羅克韋爾的實驗室在那裡我們可以每24小時測完一億字元的遺傳編碼	harvest seawater , filters different filters , gather different sizes of life , and take their dna back to the laboratory in which we can detect 100 million letters of genetic code every 24 hours .
透過這些我們已經有了一些驚人的發現	and we've made some remarkable discoveries through this .
比如我們眼睛裡的視色素之前認為自然界中只有一到兩種生物擁有和我們一樣的視色素	for instance , the visual pigments in our eyes used to think that there are only one or two species in the natural world that have the same vision of ours .
但後來發現在溫暖海區的上層海水中幾乎每個物種都擁有這類光受體並利用陽光作為能量來源和交流工具	but it turns out that in the temperatures of the upper waters , almost every species has this light receptor and uses the energy and communication tools of sunlight .
僅僅一個採集點 , 從一桶水中我們就能發現1300萬個新基因相當於5萬個新種	in a single mine , we found 13 million new genes equal to 50 , 000 new species from a single barrel .
藉助來自斯隆基金會的資助我們已經將研究擴充套件到空氣中	with funding from the sloan foundation , we've extended research into the air .
我們正在測算 , 在我們每天呼吸的空氣中漂浮著多少病毒和細菌特別是在飛機和禮堂等封閉環境中	we're working on calculations , how many viruses and bacteria are floating in the air that we breathe every day , especially in the airplanes and the auditorium .
我們透過一些簡單的儀器進行過濾在紐約市某棟建築的頂上僅用一天我們就過濾出數十億計的微生物	we filter through some simple devices on top of a building in new york city , and just one day , we filter billions of microbes .
目前我們正在對它們進行測序	we're currently sequencing them .
單純從資料蒐集方面僅僅在加拉帕戈斯群島我們就發現幾乎每200英里我們都能從採集的樣品中看到巨大的多樣性	and just from the dataset , just in the galapagos islands , we found that nearly every 200 miles we could see enormous diversity in samples .
不同的溫度梯度或許可以部分解釋這種多樣性	different temperature gradients may explain this diversity .
這是一張基於溫度的衛星圖片紅色表示溫暖區域藍色表示冷的區域我們發現 , 在溫暖海水中獲得樣品與冷海水中的樣品在物種的豐富程度上具有極大的差異	this is a satellite image based on temperature , shown in red , and the warm region shows warm , and in blue , we found that samples and samples in warm water have a significant distinction in the abundance of species .
另一個讓我們感到驚奇的事情是這些光受體能探測到不同波長的光而我們能透過它們的氨基酸序列來推測這一過程	another thing that surprised us is that these light receptors detect light at different wavelengths , and we can predict this through their amino acid sequence .
不同區域之間 , 它們也差別巨大	and they're also enormously different across different regions .
或許不是很讓人驚奇在幾乎是幽藍的深海里光受體傾向於 " 看 " 到藍光	maybe not surprisingly , in the deep sea of humor , the light receptor tends to look at the blue light .
而當週圍存在大量葉綠素的時候它們則 " 看 " 到許多綠光	and when there's a lot of chlorophyll around , they say , " look , lots of green light . "
在向較極端的紅外和紫外波段移動時光受體的差別可能更大	in terms of moving towards extreme infrared and ultraviolet , the difference between a light receptor might be even larger .
為了對我們採集的所有基因進行評估我們彙總了所有資料包括到目前為止考察所得的所有資料代表了地球上超過一半的基因資料總共約2900萬個基因	in order to assess all of the genes we've collected , we've combined all the data , including all of the data we've collected , including all of the data we've collected , including all of the data we've collected , inc
我們把這些基因放入基因家族中試圖回答:我們是發現了已知基因家族中的新成員還是發現了新的基因家族 ?	we took those genetic families and we tried to answer them: did we discover new members of the genetic family , or did we discover new gene families ?
結果表明我們找到了大約5萬個主要的基因家族但我們從環境中獲得的每個新樣品都只是對這些新基因家族的線性補充	it turns out that we found about 50 , 000 major gene familys , but every new sample we take from the environment is just a linear implement for these new genetic families .
因此我們正處在發現地球生命及其組成部分和基因基礎的最初階段	so we're at the earliest stages of discovering life on earth and its components and its genetic base .
我們來看下所謂的進化樹我們人類就在右上角 , 和動物們在一起	so let's look at what's called an evolutionary tree , and we humans are up in the upper righthand corner with animals .
在動物界約2900萬個基因中我們的基因組才僅僅擁有24000個基因	in the animal kingdom , we only have about 24 , 000 genes .
如果把所有的動物算在一起我們與之分享著不到30000可能在1.2萬或再多數千的不同的基因家族	if we counted all the animals together , we shared less than 3 , 000 genetic families with each other , at 1 . 2 million , 000 , or thousands of different genetic families .
現在我不僅僅將這些基因視為進化的設計元件	now , i'm not just looking at these genes as design components of evolution .
而且我們要從 " 基因中心觀點 " 或許要追溯到理查德•道金斯的理論而非 " 基因組中心觀點 " 來思考它們對這些基因元件的構造方式是不同的	and we're going to go from a genecentric viewpoint to something like richard dawkins' theory , rather than the central view of the genome , to thinking about their constructs in terms of the components of these genes .
合成dna , 即人工合成dna的能力在過去的十年或二十年裡與dna測序的能力在某種程度上是同步發展的而且都變得越來越快速和廉價	synthetic dna , the ability to synthesize dna , has been increasingly fast and cheap for the last 10 years or 20 years with dna sequencing , has been increasingly synthesized .
有關合成基因組的想法是在1995年我們對第二個基因組即生殖道支原體測序的時候想到的	the idea of the synthetic genome is that in 1995 , we came to think about the second genitalia , the genitalia sequencing .
我們還製作了相當不錯的t恤寫著 , " 我愛惜我的生殖器 "	we also made a pretty good tshirt , which says , " i love my genitalia . "
這其實只不過是個微小的生物	it's just a small creature .
卻擁有近500個基因	they have almost 500 genes .
嗜血桿菌擁有1800個基因	haemophilus has 1 , 800 genes .
我們提出疑問如果某物種需要800個基因 , 另一種需要500個是否能用一套更小的基因組成一個微小的可運作生命系統	and we asked , if one species needs 800 genes , another one , whether 500 of them can use one smaller set of genomes , one small , operating system .
於是我們開始做轉座子的突變發生	so we started working on the mutations of the seats .
轉座子是隨機插入遺傳編碼之中的短的dna片段	the nuclear seat is a short piece of dna that randomly inserts the genetic code .
如果轉座子插入到基因中間 , 就會擾亂基因的功能	if you insert a seat in the gene , it disrupts the function of the gene .
因此我們找出所有能夠接受轉座子插入的基因併為這些 " 非必需基因 " 製作了 " 地圖 "	so we figured out all the genes that could transmit instructions to make these " nonnecessary genes . "
但結果我們發現環境對此的影響非常關鍵我們只能根據環境中確實存在的條件來定義必需和非必需基因	but it turns out that the environment matters a lot , and we can only define the necessity and nonnegative genes based on the conditions that actually exist in the environment .
我們還試圖做一個更直觀的研究對13個有親緣關係的生物我們試圖比較它們的基因組 , 看它們是否有相同之處	we also tried to make a more intuitive study of 13 intimate creatures , and we tried to compare their genomes to see if they had the same thing .
於是我們得到了這些重疊的圓圈 , 我們發現只有173個基因在這所有13種生物中是相同的	so we got these overlapping circles , and we found that only 173 genes are the same for all 13 species .
如果忽略掉一個細胞內寄生物的話這個基因庫還能擴充套件一點當我們審視核心的一組約310個基因時基因庫擴大更多	if we ignore a parasite inside a cell , the gene pool can also spread a bit , and when we look at a core of about 310 genes , the gene bank expands even more .
因此我們認為可以從最少500個基因擴充套件或縮小取決你怎麼看這個問題到約300到400個基因	so we thought that we could go from the minimal 500 gene expansions or shrinks , how do you look at this problem , to about 300 to 400 genes .
證明這些理論的唯一方法是以這些基因人工構建一個染色體而且我們必須用基於表達框的方式來達到這一目的	the only way to prove that these theories are by making a chromosome out of these genes , and we have to do that on a frameworkbased basis .
我們發現大片段精確合成dna是非常非常困難的	it turns out that big pieces of synthesizing dna are really hard .
我的同事漢姆•史密斯和克萊德•哈欽森發明了一個讓人振奮的新方法能讓我們在短短兩週時間內合成一個擁有5000個鹼基對的病毒而且在基因序列和生物學特性上都百分百精確	my colleague ham smith and krightson invented an exciting new way that we can synthesize a virus with 50 , 000 base pairs of viruses in just two weeks , and 100 percent accurate within the gene sequence and the properties of biology .
那是個相當讓人興奮的實驗:我們僅僅把合成的dna片段注進細菌中 , 突然之間dna就開始引導病毒顆粒的合成而病毒反過來殺死了細菌	it was a very exciting experiment: we just inserted a synthetic piece of dna into the bacteria , and all of a sudden , the dna started to introduce the synthetic particles of the virus , and the virus was going to come and kill the bacteria .
這並非第一個合成的病毒一年前已有某種脊髓灰質炎病毒被製造了出來但這卻是唯一達到百分之一活性的病毒耗時三年才合成成功	this isn't the first synthetic virus that had been produced just a year ago , but it was the only threeyear time success that it took three years to achieve .
這是phix-174結構的一個動畫	this is an animation of the phi x 174 structure .
這是軟體為自己構建硬體的活例子也為我們的生物學提供了新想法	this is the live example of software that builds its own hardware , and it provides new ideas for our biology .
有人立即開始擔心生物武器的威脅不久前我也在參議院委員會和另一個由美國政府成立旨在評價這一領域的特殊委員會上作證	someone immediately started worrying about the threat of biological weapons , and not long ago , i was at the senate committee and another american government , which was established at a special committee in this area .
我認為最重要的是將事實牢記在心而非人們對事情發生的想象	i think the most important thing is to remember the facts rather than the impressions of what happens .
基本上 , 任何現在已經被測序的病毒其基因組都可以被合成	basically , any virus that's being sequenced right now can be synthesized in its genome .
人們立馬被埃博拉病毒或天花病毒之類等嚇壞了但從這些生物體中提取的dna並不具有感染力	people were horrified by things like ebola or smallpox , but the dna extracted from these organisms was not infected .
因此即使有人制成了天花病毒基因組其dna本身並不會引發感染	so even if somebody made a smallpox genome , the dna itself doesn't cause infection .
安全部門真正需要擔心的是 " 設計者病毒 "	the security department really needs to worry about " designer virus . "
只有兩個國家 , 美國和前蘇聯曾經花大力氣致力於生物武器的研製	only two countries , the u . s . and the former soviet union , have spent an effort in biological weapons .
如果這些研究真的已經終止那麼在未來人為製造出設計者病毒的機率微乎其微	and if these studies have really ended , it's very likely that the chances of generating designer viruses for the future are very , very small .
我想兩年內製造出單細胞生物是可能的	i think it's possible to create singlecell organisms in two years .
而真核細胞我們自己擁有的這種細胞也可能在十年內製造出來	and the nuclear cell , the kind of cell that we own , can be built in a decade .
我們可以區分開進入這個人工基因組的不同表達框和不同基因使得我們能構建數十種不同的結構	we can separate into the different frames and different genes of the artificial genome , and allow us to construct dozens of different structures .
關鍵是 , 如何把所有其他的放進來 ?	the key is , how do you get all the others in there ?
我們從這些片段開始然後透過一個同源重組系統將其組合到染色體中	we start with these clips , and we combine them together through a homologous recombination system to the chromosome .
這來自一種名為耐輻射奇異球菌的生物能在三百萬拉德的輻射劑量下保持活力	this comes from an organism called deinococcus radiodurans that remain energetic at three million radical doses of radiation .
在暴露輻射約12到24小時其染色體幾乎完全破碎的情況下它還能將自身的染色體重新組裝起來	in exposure to radiation for about 12 to 24 hours , the chromosome was virtually broken , and it could reassemble its own chromosome .
這種生物在地球上幾乎無處不在甚至由於人類的活動它們還可能在外太空活動	these organisms are virtually everywhere on earth , and because of human activity , they may even be active in space .
這是玻璃燒杯在約50萬拉德輻射下的情形	this is the bottom line of the glass beaker , about half a million rads of radiation .
玻璃開始燃燒 , 爆裂而位於底部的微生物則似乎越來越開心	glass started burning and burning , and the microbes on the bottom seemed to be getting happier .
這是實際的情形上面是經過170萬拉德輻射之後的染色體	this is the actual scenario ; it's a chromosome after 17 million rads of radiation .
幾乎已經支離破碎	it's almost broken .
下面是24小時之後同樣的dna自動重組的結果	the bottom is 24 hours later , the same dna automatically reassembled .
這些生物能做到的真是歎為觀止 。 如果不是數以萬計的話也許我們還能找到數以千計的物種也同樣能夠做到	what all these organisms can do is they're really extraordinary . and if not tens of thousands , maybe we can find thousands of other species , too .
這些基因組合成之後第一步就是將它們移植到另一個沒有基因組的細胞中	the first step in combining these genomes is transplanting them into cells without another genome .
因此我們認為合成細胞將具有巨大的前景不僅僅在生物學基礎的理解上而且很可能幫我們應對環境和社會問題	so we think synthetic cells will have huge prospects , not just for biologybased understanding , but they're very likely to help us respond to environmental and social problems .
例如 , 從我們測序的第三種生物詹氏甲烷球菌 , 生活在相當於水沸點的高溫中以氫作為能量來源並依靠捕獲環境中的二氧化碳為自己提供所需的碳	for instance , methane bacteria , which we sequenced , live alcohol , equivalent to the boiling temperature equivalent to hydrogen as a source of energy , and rely on carbon dioxide in the environment to provide themselves the carbon .
由此可知 , 透過大量不同的途徑數以千計的生物能夠捕獲並依賴二氧化碳生存	so , you know , through a lot of different pathways , thousands of organisms are capable of capturing and depending on co2 .
因此我們可以透過捕獲大氣中的碳製造生物高聚物或其他產品來替代從石油中工業合成的碳製品	so we can replace the carbon from our industry by catching carbon from our atmosphere , or our polymers or other products from oil .
有種依賴一氧化碳的生物我們利用其還原能力使水分子破裂 , 製造出氫和氧	there are organisms that depend on carbon monoxide that we use to recover the water molecules and make hydrogen and oxygen .
同樣 , 還有許多途徑能夠用來轉化甲烷	similarly , there are many other ways to translate methane .
杜邦公司和挪威石油公司有一大型專案就是把挪威油氣田中的甲烷轉化為有用的產品	dupont and norway oil companies have a big program of converting methane from norway into useful products .
我突然想到 , 將有一個新的領域 " 組合基因組學 " 很快就要誕生因為有了這些新的合成方法有了這麼龐大的基因序列和同源重組我們可以設計出一個能夠每天生產近百萬個染色體的機器人	and it occurred to me that with a new field called combinatoric genomics , it was about to come up very quickly , because with these new synthesis methods , with these huge gene sequences and synthesis so we could design a robot that could produce nearly a million chromosomes a day .
因此 , 所有的生物學特徵都能透過螢幕來選擇無論是製造氫化學合成 , 或者僅僅是生存能力	so , all biological features can be chosen by screens , whether it's generating hydrogen synthesis , or just the ability to survive .
理解這些基因的功能將變得觸手可及	understanding the function of these genes is touchable .
我們正嘗試改進光合作用以直接在陽光下製造出氫	we're trying to improve photosynthesis to make hydrogen directly in the sun .
光合作用受氧調節而我們使用的對氧不敏感的氫化酶將完全改變這一過程	photosynthesis uses oxygen modulation , and the unsensitive hydrogenase we use will completely change that process .
我們還整合了多種纖維素酶這些酶可以把複雜的糖類分解為簡單的糖類並在同一個細胞內發酵產生酒精	we also integrate multiple cellulose enzymes , enzymes that break down complex sugars into simple sugars and create alcohol within the same cell .
在一些大型的實驗室裡已經開始利用微生物進行藥品生產	in some of the big labs , we've started to make drugs out of microbes .
環境中化合物的化學比我們最好的化學家制造出來的化合物還要複雜很多	the chemical compounds in the environment are much more complicated than our best chemists can produce .
也許未來的工程物種將成為我們的食物來源能量來源環境補救手段甚至取代石化行業	perhaps future engineering species will become our food source , our environmental remedy , even replace the fossil industry .
最後讓我以道德和政策上的研究結束吧	let me end with moral and policy research .
我們推遲了1999年開始的實驗直到對是否應該嘗試製造人工物種這一問題進行了一年半的生物倫理學討論後實驗才繼續進行	we late 1999 , and we launched the experiments , and it was only a year and a half of bioethical discussions that were conducted .
每個主要宗教都參與其中	every major religion participates .
真是一項奇怪的研究因為許多宗教領袖都以他們的教義、經文作為法律而且不能從中找出禁止製造生命的條文所以這應該沒什麼問題最根本的擔憂來自生物武器方面但只有開始進行這些實驗之後我們才能找出從事這一切的原因	really a strange study , because many religious leaders have used their creed , their scripture and couldn't find the criteria to prohibit life , and so that's probably the most essential concern that comes from biological weapons , but only by doing these experiments , we'll be able to figure out what's going on .
目前斯隆基金會已經資助了一個相關的多機構參與的研究以確定這些實驗給社會帶來的風險和益處同時也為像我們這樣的科學團隊在這一領域開展研究制定規則在前進的同時我們也努力成為一個良好的榜樣	now , the sloan foundation has funded a multiinstitutional study to make sure that these experiments give the risks and benefits of society , and also that they're developing the rules forward in this field , and we're trying to be a good role model .
有許多複雜的議題	there's a lot of complex issues .
除了生物恐怖主義它們其實都很簡單:我們能否設計出生產清潔能源的工具透過各種不同的簡單步驟或能徹底改變發展中國家的能源生產模式	besides bioterrorism , they're actually simple: can we design the tools to produce clean energy in a wide variety of simple steps , radically changing the energy production patterns in the developing world .
心理學家philipzimbardo說我們大部分人都忽略了幸福和成功的來源:那就是我們觀望過去、面向現在和展望未來 。 要想改善生活質量 , 他建議我們首先要調整時間觀念 。	the psychologist philip zimbardo says that most of us are missing the source of happiness and success , and that's what we look at the past , look at the present and look at the future , and to try to improve the quality of life , he recommends that we first adjust to the

我想跟你們分享一些對時間的神秘力量的看法當然是在很短的時間內	i'd like to share with you some mysterious ideas about time , in a very short time .

生活中充滿了誘惑 。 而且到處都是:屈服或反抗是、不是、現在、隨後、衝動、沉穩專注現在和展望未來	life is full of temptations , and everywhere: submission , rebellion , not , present , urge , urge , urge , steady focus , present and look towards the future .
激情時刻一旦到來 , 道德束縛將皆被打破	once the passionate moments arrive , the moral restraint will be broken .

他們等不了 。 當然 , 其它的孩子都得到了第二個棉花糖	they can't wait . of course , the other kids get the second marshmallow .

他們自信而且果斷 。 那麼今天我所要說的關鍵是同樣也是你們的關鍵點就是由 " 面向現在 " 轉變為 " 展望未來 "	the key to what i'm going to talk about today is also the key to your aspects of the present , and that is the shift to looking at the future .
那什麼是時間洞察力呢 ? 這將是我下面要講的	so what is time insight ?
時間洞察力是研究個人包括我們在內 , 如何以時間區域或時間類別為單位劃分自身的經歷體驗 。	time insight is about researching individuals , including ourselves , how to divide their experiences in time zones and time categories .
其實我們一直都在自然而然地做著	we've been doing it just naturally .
而影響我們劃分方式的因素有很多 , 包括不同的文化背景、國家個人、社會階層以及不同的教育背景	and there are many factors that influence how we zoom out , including different backgrounds , individuals , social classes , and different backgrounds of education .
問題是由於這些因素的存在 , 最終導致時間洞察力都具是片面的因為你學會經常使用其中的一些 , 而其他的則被很少使用	the problem is that there's a lot of these factors that eventually lead to insight in terms of insight , because you learn to use a lot of them , and others are rarely used .

對於那些基於現狀而做決定的人我們稱呼他們為: " 面向現在 " 因為他們專注於現正發生的事情	for those of us who make the decisions based on the status quo , we call them , " perspective , " because they focus on what's happening now .
對於另一些人來說 , 現正發生什麼並不重要	for others , it doesn't matter what's happening right now .
就好像是說: " 我以前好像經歷過類似的事情 " 一樣	it's like , " i've experienced something like this before . "
所以 , 他們基於過去的經驗來做決定	so they make decisions based on past experience .
我們稱呼這些人為: " 觀望過去 " , 因為他們專注於過去	we call these people " look past , " because they're focused on the past .
還有一部分人 , 他們的考慮不是基於現在 , 也不是過去而是未來	and then there's another group of people whose minds are not based on present , not in the past , but in the future .
他們專注於預期的結果	they focused on the expected outcome .
我們稱呼這些人為:展望未來 。 因為他們專注於將來會是怎麼樣的	we call these people: to look forward to the future , because they focus on what the future will look like .

於是他們沒有放棄	so they didn't give up .
以色列有一個新的和平運動被稱為 " 索裡德拉爾特 " 在希伯來語中意為 " 團結一致 "	israel has a new peace movement referred to as " solidarity , " which means " solidarity " in hebrew .
佈德魯斯的故事成為了這個運動的領導者招兵買馬的主要手段之一	the story of budrus is one of the main means of recruiting horses in the campaign .
他們反映說那些從未加入任何運動的以色列人看了紀錄片之後瞭解了非暴力抵抗的力量並開始加入他們行動	they reflection that israelis who had never looked at the movies , understood the power of nonviolent resistance and started joining them .
瓦拉傑和索裡德拉爾特運動的例子告訴我們即使是小成本的獨立電影也能夠幫助非暴力抵抗轉變為一種功能性行為	valrajah and solidariot movements have shown that even a smallbudget independent film can help nonviolent resistance turn into a functional behavior .
想象一下主流媒體若是開始報道每週在貝拉因尼亞林瓦拉傑等村莊以及耶路撒冷境內的香克哈拉和西路萬巴勒斯坦居住區裡發生的非暴力示威活動這將產生多麼巨大的力量更多的人會關注非暴力運動領導者重視他們讓他們的工作更有成效	imagine if mainstream media started to report , every week in villages like berlinia lynia valerje and in jerusalem , quekhara and the nonviolent demonstrations in the neighborhood of palestine and nonviolence in the neighborhood , and more people would pay attention to nonviolent leaders , and more people would pay attention to their work more effectively .
我相信最重要的是我們要認識到如果我們不關注這些運動它們就是隱形的彷彿從來沒有發生過	and i think the most important thing is that we have to recognize that if we don't pay attention to these movements , they're invisible .
但我以親身經歷為證如果我們關注這些運動就會得到發展	but i have a personal experience , and if we pay attention , it's going to happen .
它們一旦發展其影響力就會遍及巴以衝突	once they develop its influence , they can spread through a conflict .
這種影響能夠最終將衝突化解	this is the ultimate breakdown of conflict .
這些領導者證明了非暴力運動在佈德魯斯這樣的地方是可行的	these leaders have demonstrated that nonviolent movements like dress are possible in places like bodrus .
我們一起來關注他們讓他們證明這在任何地方都是可行的	and together , they made them prove that this could work everywhere .
西蒙•斯涅克用一個簡單但是震撼的模型來闡釋激勵人心的領袖力 , 這個模型的核心是一個 " 黃金 " 圓圈 , 意思是領袖素質的根本來源是回答 " 為什麼 ? " 。 他列舉了蘋果公司、馬丁•路德•金還有萊特兄弟成功的例子 , 同時以蒂沃數碼錄影機為失敗的典型 。 雖然蒂沃最近打贏一場官司 , 使得其股價上漲了3倍 , 但是它仍在掙扎中 。	simone sneaker uses a simple but shocking model to illustrate the power of inspiring leaders , a model at the core of a golden circle , which means the quality of a leader is answering , " why ? " he told examples of apple companies , martin luther king and the wright brothers , and the typical failure of a digital digital video camera , although watty's last winning a stack loss , which still has doubled .
bullseye , business , entrepreneur , leadership , sales , selling , success	bullseye , entrepreneur . sales , sales , selling , ccess .
西蒙•斯涅克:偉大的領袖如何激勵行動	simon stanek: how great leaders inspired action .
當事情的發展出乎意料之外的時候 , 你怎麼解釋 ?	how do you explain when things are surprising and surprising ?
換句話說 , 當別人似乎出乎意料地取得成功的時候 , 你怎麼解釋 ?	in other words , how do you explain when someone seems to have a success that is unexpectedly unexpected ?
比如說 , 為什麼蘋果公司創新能力這麼強 ?	for example , why are apples so innovative ?
這麼多年來 , 年復一年 , 他們比所有競爭對手都更加具有創新性 。	over the years , year after year , they're more innovative than all competitors .
而其實他們只是一家電腦公司 。	and they're really just a computer company .
他們跟其他公司沒有任何分別 ,	they're not separated from the other companies .
有同樣的途徑 , 接觸到同樣的人才 , 同樣的代理商 , 顧問 , 和媒體 。	there's the same path , touching the same talent , the same proxy merchant , advisor and media .
那為什麼他們就似乎有那麼一點不同尋常呢 ?	so why do they seem to be slightly different ?
同樣的 , 為什麼是由馬丁•路德•金來領導民權運動 ?	and again , why is it the civil rights movement , martin luther king ?
那個時候在美國 , 民權運動之前 , 不僅僅只有他一個人飽受歧視 。 他也決不是那個時代唯一的偉大演說家 。	at the time in the united states , before the civil rights movement , it wasn't just himself rising discriminators , it was also not the only great orator of his time .
又為什麼懷特兄弟能夠造出動力控制的載人飛機 , 跟他們相比 , 當時的其他團隊似乎更有能力 , 更有資金 ,	and why the white brothers were able to create motivational , controlled airplanes , which seemed to be more capable , more financially , compared to the rest of the team at the time .
他們卻沒能製造出載人飛機 , 懷特兄弟打敗了他們 。	they didn't make a carrier plane and the white brothers beat them .
一定還有一些什麼別的因素在起作用 。	there must be something else that works there .
大概三年半之前 , 我有了個新發現 ,	about three and a half years ago , i made a discovery .
這個發現完全改變了我對這個世界如何運作的看法 。 甚至從根本上改變了我的工作生活方式 。	this discovery completely changed my view of how the world works , and even fundamentally changed the way i work in my work life .
那就是我發現了一種模式 ,	and that's what i discovered .
我發現世界上所有偉大的令人振奮的領袖和組織 , 無論是蘋果公司、馬丁•路德•金還是懷特兄弟 , 他們思考、行動、交流溝通的方式都完全一樣 ,	i discovered that all of the world's great leaders and organizations , whether it's apple , whether it's martin luther king or the white brothers , are thinking , action , communicating in exactly the same way .
但是跟所有其他人的方式完全相反 。	but the opposite is the opposite of everyone else .
我所做的僅僅是把它整理出來 。 這可能是世上最簡單的概念 。	all i'm doing is cleaning it up , and that's probably the easiest thing in the world .
我稱它為黃金圓環 。	i call it the golden circle .
為什麼 ? 怎麼做 ? 是什麼 ?	why ? what ?
這小小的模型就解釋了為什麼一些組織和領導者能夠在別人不能的地方激發出靈感和潛力 。	this little model explains why some organizations and leaders can inspire inspiration and potential where others can't .
我來儘快地解釋一下這些術語 。	let me explain the terminology as quickly as possible .
地球上的每個人 , 每個組織都明白自己做的是什麼 , 百分之百 。	every single person on the planet understands what they're doing , 100 percent .
其中一些知道該怎麼做 , 你可以稱之為是你的差異價值 , 或是你的獨特工藝 , 或是你的獨特賣點也好 , 怎麼說都行 。	some of them know what to do , which you could call your differences , or your unique craftsmanships , or your unique trade points , or whatever you're doing .
但是非常 , 非常少的人和組織明白為什麼做 。	but very , very few people and organizations know why .
這裡的 " 為什麼 " 和 " 為利潤 " 沒有關係 ,	the " why " and " profit " doesn't matter .
利潤只是一個結果 , 永遠只能是一個結果 。	profit is just one outcome , it can only be one outcome .
我說的 " 為什麼 " 指的是:你的目的是什麼 ?	and by " why " i mean: what is your goal ?
你這樣做的原因是什麼 ? 你懷著什麼樣的信念 ?	what is the reason you're doing that ? what kind of beliefs are you preserving ?
你的機構為什麼而存在 ?	why does your institution exist ?
你每天早上是為什麼而起床 ?	why did you wake up every morning ?
為什麼別人要在乎你 ?	why do people care about you ?
結果是 , 我們思考的方式 , 行動的方式 , 交流的方式都是由外向內的 。	it turns out that the way we think , the way we act , the way we communicate is by extroverts .
很顯然的 , 我們所採用的方式是從清晰開始 , 然後到模糊的東西 。	obviously , the way we do it is by starting with clarity and blurry stuff .
但是激勵型領袖以及組織機構 , 無論他們的規模大小 , 所在領域 , 他們思考 , 行動和交流的方式都是從裡向外的 。	but inspired by inspiring leaders and organizations , both in their scale and in their discipline , they think and act and communicate exclusively .
舉個例子吧 。	let me give you an example .
我舉蘋果公司是因為這個例子簡單易懂 , 每個人都能理解 。	i hold apple because it's an example that everybody can understand .
如果蘋果公司跟其他公司一樣 , 他們的市場營銷資訊就會是這個樣子: " 我們做最棒的電腦 ,	if apple was like any other company , their marketing information would look like this: " we make the best computer .
設計精美 , 使用簡單 , 介面友好 。	design beauty using simple interfaces .
你想買一臺嗎 ? " 不怎麼樣吧 。	you want to buy one ? " not so much .
這就是我們大多數人的交流方式 ,	this is how most of us communicate .
也是大多數市場推廣的方式 , 大部分銷售所採用的方式 , 也是我們大部分人互相交流的方式 。	it's also the way most markets work , most of the ways that sales work , and the way most of us talk to each other .
我們說我們的職業是幹什麼的 , 我們說我們是如何的與眾不同 , 或者我們怎麼比其他人更好 , 然後我們就期待著一些別人的反應 , 比如購買 , 比如投票 , 諸如此類 。	we say what our profession does , we say that we're extraordinarily different or how we're better than everyone else , and then we expect some people's reactions , like buying a vote , and so on and so forth .
這是我們新開的的律師事務所 , 我們擁有最棒的律師和最大的客戶 , 我們總是能滿足客戶的要求 。	this is our new law firm , and we have the best lawyers and the biggest clients , and we're always meeting the requirements of our clients .
這是我們的新車型 , 非常省油 , 真皮座椅 。 買一輛吧 。	this is our new vehicle , very cheap , derriet chair . get one .
這是蘋果公司實際上的溝通方式:	this is how apple actually communicates .
" 我們做的每一件事情 , 都是為了突破和創新 。	" everything we do is for breakthroughs and innovation .
我們堅信應該以不同的方式思考 。	we firmly believe that we should think differently .
我們挑戰現狀的方式是透過把我們的產品設計得十分精美 , 使用簡單 , 和介面友好 。	the way we challenge the status quo is by designing our products perfectly beautifully , using simple , interfaces friendly .
我們只是在這個過程中做出了最棒的電腦 。	we just made the best computer in the process .
想買一臺嗎 ? "	want to buy one ? "
感覺完全不一樣 , 對吧 ? 你已經準備從我這裡買一臺了 。	feel completely different , right ? you're ready to buy one from me .
我所做的只是將傳遞資訊的順序顛倒一下而已 。	what i did was i turned the sequence of information upside down .
事實已經向我們證明 , 人們買的不是你做的產品 , 人們買的是你的信念和宗旨 。	it has proven to us that people don't buy products that you make , and people buy your beliefs and gospels .
人們買的不是你做的產品 , 人們買的是你的信念 。	people don't buy products that you make ; people buy your beliefs .
這就解釋了為什麼這裡的每個人從蘋果公司買電腦時都覺得理所當然 。	which explains why everyone here has to take it for granted when they're buying a computer from an apple .
但是我們從蘋果公司買mp3播放器 , 手機 , 或者數碼攝像機時 , 也感覺很舒服 。	but we bought mp3 players from apple , phones , digital cameras , too .
而其實 , 我剛才已經說過 , 蘋果公司只是個電腦公司 。	and as i've already said , apple's just a computer company .
沒有什麼能從結構上將蘋果公司同競爭對手區分開來 。	there's nothing that separates apple's competitive competition from the structure .
競爭對手和蘋果公司有同樣的能力製造所有這些產品 。	competition makes the same thing as apple makes all of these products .
實際上 , 他們也嘗試過 。	in fact , they've tried .
幾年前 , 捷威公司推出了平板電視 。	a few years ago , the czero agency introduced a tablet .
他們製造平板電視的能力很強 ,	they have a strong ability to make tablets .
因為他們做平板顯示器已經很多年了 。	because they've been working on the tablets for years .
戴爾公司推出了mp3播放器和掌上電腦 , 他們產品的質量非常好 , 產品的設計也非常不錯 。 但是也沒有人買他們的這些產品 。	dale launched mp3 players and palmpilots , and the mass of their products was very good , the design of their products was very good , and nobody bought them .
其實 , 說到這裡 , 我們無法想象會從戴爾公司買mp3播放器 。	well , speaking of that , we can't imagine buying an mp3 player from dell .
你為什麼會從一家電腦公司買mp3播放器呢 ?	why would you buy an mp3 player from a computer company ?
但是每天我們都這麼做 。	but we do it every day .
人們買的不是你做的產品 , 人們買的是你的信念 。	people don't buy products that you make ; people buy your beliefs .
做公司的目標不是要跟所有需要你的產品的人做生意 ,	the goal of the company is not to trade with everybody who needs your product .
而是跟與你有著相同理念的人做生意 。	it's about doing business with people who share your ideas .
這是最精彩的部分 。 我說的這些沒有一個是我自己的觀點 。	that's the best part . none of these things i'm talking about are my own perspective .
這些觀點都能從生物學裡面找到根源 。	these views can be found in biology .
不是心理學 , 是生物學 。	it's not psychology , it's biology .
當你俯視看大腦的橫截面 , 你會發現人類大腦實際上分成三個主要部分 , 而這三個主要部分和黃金圓環匹配得非常好 。	when you look at the crosssection of the brain , you realize that the human brain actually has three key components , and those three main components are very well matched with golden circles .
我們最新的腦部 , 管轄智力的腦部 , 或者說我們的大腦皮層 , 對應著 " 是什麼 " 這個圓環 。	our newest brain , our jurisdictional brain , or our neocortex , corresponds to the " what " circle .
大腦皮層負責我們所有的理性和邏輯的思考和語言功能 。	the neocortex is responsible for all of our rational and logical thinking and functioning of language .
中間的兩個部分是我們的兩個邊腦 。 邊腦負責我們所有的情感 , 比如信任和忠誠 ,	the two parts in the middle are our two sides of our brain , and our brain is responsible for all of our emotions , like trust and loyalty .
也負責所有的行為和決策 , 但這部分沒有語言功能 。	it's also responsible for all behaviors and decisions , but it doesn't have linguistic functions .
換句話說 , 當我們由外向內交流時 , 沒錯 , 人們可以理解大量的複雜資訊 , 比如特徵 , 優點 , 事實和圖表 。	in other words , when we're extroverted inwards , yes , people can understand lots of complex information , like features , facts and graphics .
但不足以激發行動 。	but it's not enough to spark action .
當我們由內向外交流時 , 我們是在直接同控制行為的那一部分大腦對話 , 然後我們由人們理性地思考我們所說和做的事情 。	when we're introverted , we're talking to the part of the brain that's directly controlling the behavior , and then we're rationally thinking about what we're saying and doing .
這就是那些發自內心的決定的來源 。	that's where the internal decisions come from .
你知道 , 有時候你展示給一些人所有的資料圖表 , 他們會說 " 我知道這些資料和圖表是什麼意思 , 但就是感覺不對 。 "	you know , sometimes you show all the data graphs to some people , and they say , " i know what this data and graph means , but it just doesn't feel right . "
為什麼我們會用這個動詞 , " 感覺 " 不對 ?	why do we use that verb , that feeling ?
因為控制決策的那一部分大腦並不支配語言 ,	because the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking is not part of the brain .
我們只好說 " 我不知道為什麼 , 就是感覺不對 。 "	we're just going to say , " i don't know why , just don't feel right . "
或者有些時候 , 你說聽從心的召喚 , 或者說聽從靈魂 。	or in some cases , you can hear the calling from the heart , or you can hear from the soul .
我不想把這些觀念分解得太徹底 , 但心和靈魂都不是控制行為的部分 。	i don't want to break these ideas down too thoroughly , but the heart and soul are not part of the behavioral and controlled effort .
所有這一切都發生在你的邊腦 , 控制決策行為而非語言的邊腦 。	all of this happens to your side , to control decisionmaking behavior rather than language .
如果你自己都不知道你為什麼幹你所做的事情 , 而別人要對你的動機作出反應 , 那麼你怎麼可能贏得大家對你的支援 , 從你這裡購買東西 , 或者 , 更重要的 , 對你忠誠並且想成為你正在做的事情的一分子呢 ?	if you don't know why you do what you do , and people respond to your motivations , then how can you possibly get your support , buy things from you , or , more importantly , be loyal to you and want to be part of what you're doing ?
再說一次 , 目標不僅僅是將你有的東西賣給需要它們的人 ; 而是將東西賣給跟你有共同信念的人 。	again , the aim is not just sold to the people who need it ; it's selling to the people who share your beliefs .
目標不僅僅是僱傭那些需要一份工作的人 ; 目標是僱傭那些同你有共同信念的人 。	the goal is not just to hire servants those who need a job ; the goal is to hire people who share faith with you .
你知道嗎 , 我總是說 , 如果你僱傭某人只是因為他能做這份工作 , 他們就只是為你開的工資而工作 , 但是如果你僱傭跟你有共同信念的人 , 他們會為你付出熱血 , 汗水和淚水 。	you know , i always say , if you hire someone for this work , they're just working for the wages you have , but if you hire people who share your beliefs , they will give you bleeds and sweat and tears .
這一點 , 沒有比懷特兄弟的故事更恰當的例子了 。	and that's not even appropriate for the story of the white brothers .
大多數人都沒聽說過塞繆爾•蘭利這個人 。	most people haven't heard about this guy , cermeir langley .
20世紀初期 , 投入機動飛行器的熱情就像當今的網站熱 ,	in the early 20th century , the passion for flying aerial robots was like websites today .
每個人都在做嘗試 。	everyone was trying .
塞繆爾•蘭利擁有所有大家認為是成功的要素 。	samuel langley has all the ingredients that people think of as success .
我的意思是 , 即便是現在 , 你問別人 " 為什麼你的產品或者公司失敗了呢 ? "	i mean , even now , you ask people , " why is your product or your company failing ? "
人們總是用同樣的三個東西以同樣的排列順序來回答你 , 缺乏資金 , 用人不善 , 形勢不好 。	people are always answering you in the same three things , in the same order , lack of funding , lack of improvement , dysfunction .
總是那三種理由 , 所以讓我們來逐個分析一下 。	there are three reasons why , so let's go through one analysis .
國防部給了塞繆爾•蘭利5萬美金作為研製飛行器的資金 。	the department of defense has given samuel langley 50 , 000 dollars as a funding to build aircraft .
所以說 , 資金不是問題 。	so , funding is not the problem .
他在哈佛大學工作過 , 也在史密森尼學會工作過 , 人脈極其廣泛 。 他認識當時最優秀的人才 。	he's worked at harvard university , and he's worked at the smithsonian school , and he knows the best people at the time .
因此 , 他僱傭了用資金能吸引到的最優秀的人才 。 當時的市場形勢相當有利 。	so he hired the best people to attract in funding , and the market conditions were terribly powerful .
紐約時報對他做跟蹤報道 , 每個人都支援他 。	the new york times reported and tracked him , and everybody supported him .
但是為什麼你們連聽都沒聽說過他呢 ?	but why haven't you heard about him ?
與此同時 , 幾百公里之外的俄亥俄州代頓市有一對兄弟 , 奧維爾•萊特和維爾伯•萊特 , 他們倆沒有任何我們認為的成功的要素 。	at the same time , hundreds of kilometers away in ohio city , there was a brother and a couple of brothers , alvire wright and wilbert wright , and they didn't have the ingredients to succeed that way .
他們沒有錢 。 他們用腳踏車店的收入來追求他們的夢想 。 萊特兄弟的團隊中沒有一個人上過大學 , 就連奧維爾和維爾伯也沒有 。 紐約時報更是不沾邊的 。	they had no money . they used a bicycle revenue to pursue their dreams . none of the wright brothers had gone to college , and none of the new york times had ever gone to college .
不同的是 , 奧維爾和維爾伯追求的是一個事業 , 一個目標 , 一種信念 。	what was different was that orville and wilbur were looking for an enterprise , a goal , a belief .
他們相信如果他們能研製出飛行器 , 將會改變全世界的發展程序 。	they believed that if they could develop an aircraft , it would change the course of the world .
塞繆爾•蘭利就不同了 ,	samuel langley was different .
他想要發財 , 他想要成名 。	he wanted to make money , and he wanted to be famous .
他追求的是最終結果 ,	he was looking for the ultimate results .
是變得富有 。	it's becoming rich .
看吧 , 看接下來怎麼樣了 。	see what happens next .
那些懷有和懷特兄弟一樣夢想的人跟他們一起熱血朝天地奮鬥著 。	those who are as dreamed as the white brothers , with their blood struggling with them .
另一邊的人則是為了工資而工作 。	on the other side , people work for salary .
後來流傳的故事說 , 每次懷特兄弟出去實驗時 , 都必須帶著五組零件 , 因為那是在他們回來吃晚飯之前將要墜毀的次數 。	the story goes that every time the white brothers went out to experiment with five components , because that's the number that will crash before they return to dinner .
最後 , 在1903年12月17日 , 懷特兄弟成功起飛 , 但是當時沒有任何其他人在場目睹 。	and finally , on december 17 , 1903 , the white brothers took off , but nobody else was watching .
我們是在幾天後才知道的 。	we knew it just a few days later .
後來的事情進一步證實了蘭利動機不純 , 他在懷特兄弟成功的當天就辭職了 。	what happened further proved the langley motivation was that he resigned the day the day that the white brothers had succeeded .
他本來應該可以說: " 夥計們 , 這真是一項偉大的發明 , 我可以改進你們的技術 。 " 但是他沒有 ,	he was supposed to be able to say , " guys , this is a great invention , and i can improve your technology . "
因為他不是第一個製造出飛機的人 , 他就不會變得富有 , 他也不會變得有名 , 所以他辭職了 。	because he wasn't the first person to make an airplane , he wouldn't be rich , and he wouldn't be famous , so he quit .
人們買的不是你的產品 ; 而是你的信念 。	people buy not your product ; they buy your beliefs .
如果你講述你的信念 , 你將吸引那些跟你擁有同樣信念的人 。	and if you tell your beliefs , you're going to attract those who share your beliefs .
但是為什麼吸引那些跟你擁有同樣信念的人非常重要呢 ?	but why is it so important to attract people who believe like you ?
創新的傳播有一個規律 , 如果你不知道這個規律 , 你一定了解這個概念 。	there's a pattern in the spread of innovation , and if you don't know the pattern , you've got to understand the concept .
我們的社會中 , 有2.5%的人是革新者 。	two and a half percent of our society are revolutionaries .
13.5%的人是早期的少部分採納者 。	13 . 5 percent were a small percentage of the early adopters .
接下來的34%是早期接受的大多數 , 然後是比較晚接受的大多數和最後行動的 。	the next 34 percent is an early acceptable majority , and then most later accepts and last moves .
這部分最後行動的人買按鍵電話的唯一原因是因為他們再也買不到轉盤電話了 。	that's the only reason the people who end up buying their phone calls is because they're never going to be able to buy a call anymore .
雖然我們在不同的時候會處在這個曲線上不同的位置 , 但是創新的傳播規律告訴我們如果你想在大眾市場上獲得成功 , 或者要大眾接納一個點子 , 你得等到獲得15%-18%的市場接受度這個轉折點之後才行 。 那時之後市場才真正開啟 。	although we're in different places at different times , the distribution of innovations tells us that if you want to succeed in the public market , or to embrace an idea , you have to wait for 15 to 18 percent of the market reception points later when the market receives itself .
我喜歡問公司: " 你的新生意怎麼樣呀 ? "	i like to ask the company , " what about your new business ? "
他們會很自豪地告訴你 " 哦 , 大概有10%吧 。 "	they're proud to tell you , " oh , maybe 10 percent . "
是呀 , 你有可能就在10%的顧客群這裡過不去了 。	yeah , you might end up with maybe 10 percent of the customers here .
我們都能讓10%的人 " 意會 " ,	we can all make 10 percent of the population " consent . "
對 , 我們一般這樣形容他們 。	yeah , we generally describe them .
就好比描述那種感覺: " 哦 , 他們有點心領神會了 " 。	it's like describing that feeling , " oh , they're a little bit of a god . "
問題是:你怎麼在他們還沒有成為你的顧客之前就發現那些能意會的人 , 和那些不能意會的人 ?	the question is: how did you find those intentional people long before they were found to be your customers , those intentional people ?
這就是問題的所在 , 就是這點間隙 , 你得把這個間隙給填上 , 正如傑弗裡穆爾所說的 , " 跨越鴻溝 " 。 因為早期的大多數不會嘗試新事物 , 除非有些人已經先嚐試過了 。	and that's the problem , and that's the crack , and you need to fill this gap , and as geoffrey mull said , " cross the gap , " because the very majority of early on trying things unless some of you have tried it before .
而這些人 , 創新者和早期的少數人 , 他們喜歡大膽的嘗試 。	and these folks , the innovators and the early minorities , they love a bold attempt .
他們更自然地憑直覺做事情 , 發自於他們的世界觀的直覺 , 而不僅僅是因為市場上有什麼樣的產品 。	they do things more naturally from their intuitions of their worldview instincts , rather than just the products of what's on the market .
這是一批在iphone上市的頭幾天去排隊等六個小時來購買的人 , 而其實只要等一個星期你就可以隨便走進店裡從貨架上買到 。	this was the first day of an iphone queue for six hours on the iphone , and you could just wait a week to get into the store and buy it from the shelf .
這是一批在平板電視剛推出時會花4萬美金買一臺的人 , 儘管當時的技術還不成熟 。	this is a group of people who , when they launched on the tablet , it cost 40 , 000 dollars to buy one , despite the fact that the techniques weren't there yet .
補充說一下 , 他們並不是因為技術的先進而買那些產品 , 而是為了他們自己 。	and to put that in context , they're not buying those products because of the advancement of technology , but because of them .
因為他們想成為第一個體驗新產品的人 。	because they want to be the first one to experience a new product .
人們買的不是你的產品 ; 人們買的是你的信念 。 你的行動只是證明了你的信念 。	what people buy is not your product ; what people buy is your beliefs .
實際上 , 人們會去做能夠體現他們的信念的事情 。	in fact , people do things that express their beliefs .
那些為了搶先在頭六個小時內買到iphone而排六個小時的隊的人 , 是出於他們的世界觀 , 出於他們想別人怎麼看自己 。 他們是第一批體驗者 。	the ones who lined up for the first six hours in order to buy an iphone in the first six hours , out of their worldviews , they wanted to see themselves . they were the first ones .
人們買的不是你的產品 ; 他們買的是你的信念 。	people are not buying your product ; they buy your beliefs .
我再舉些著名的例子吧 , 證實創新傳播規律的一個失敗的例子和一個成功的例子 。	i'll give you some famous examples of how innovation has failed and a successful example .
首先我們講這個失敗的例子 。	so let's start with an example of this failure .
還是商業上的 。	it was commercial .

我們先著眼於大腦海馬區 , 即黃色的區域這是我們的記憶器官 。	let's first look at the hippocampus , the yellow area that's our memory organ .
如果海馬區出現損傷 , 像老年痴呆症患者一樣 , 你將喪失記憶力 , 乃至記不起將車停在了何處 。	if there's damage to the hippocampus , like someone with dementia , you're going to lose your memory and you're unable to park your car .
hippocampus這個詞源自拉丁語 , 有 " 海馬 " 之意因為腦中海馬區的形狀看上去有點像 " 海馬 " 。	the hippocampus comes from the latin word for " hippocampus , " because it looks a little bit like " hippocampus . "
海馬區和大腦其它區域的組成相似 , 都由神經元構成 。	the hippocampus and the rest of the brain consists of neurons .
人的大腦由大約一千億個神經元細胞組成 。	your brain consists of about 100 billion neurons in your brain .
每個神經元細胞之間透過一些連線中介互相傳送小的電脈衝或者尖峰電壓來進行 " 交流 " 。	each neuron is passing a small pulse or a spike of communication through some of these connections .
海馬區由兩層片狀的細胞群構成 , 這兩層細胞群緊密相連 。	the hippocampus is made up of two layers of cells that are intimately connected .
科學家們透過記錄老鼠在某環境中搜羅食物時其腦中單個神經元細胞的反應來了解 " 空間記憶 " 的工作原理與工作機制 。	scientists respond by recording the reactions of single neurons in their brains to understand how spatial memory works and works .
現在想象一下 , 我們正在為這隻老鼠的海馬區中的一個神經元細胞 " 錄影 " 。	now imagine that we're videotaping this neuron in the hippocampus of this mouse .
每當這個細胞發出小型尖峰電壓 , 隨後會出現一個紅點以及咔噠的一聲 。	every time this cell produces a little spiky peak pressure , a little red dot and a click .
我們可以看出每當老鼠進入環境中某一特定位置 , 這個神經元細胞便會有反應 。	we can see that every time a mouse enters a certain location in the environment , the neuron will respond .
然後這個細胞再透過小型尖峰電壓將以上資訊傳遞給大腦的其它區域 。	and then this cell , via small peak pressure , transmits all this information to other areas of the brain .
這麼一來 , 我們可以憑藉這個細胞傳送訊號的頻率推知老鼠經過的相應位置 。	so we can tell by using the frequency of this cell to send a signal to mice where it's going .
倘若我們記錄的是很多不同的神經元細胞 , 就會發現當老鼠處於不同的位置上時 , 不同的神經元細胞會產生各自的電訊號 , 正如我們在這些方形中看到的那樣 。	and if we record a lot of different neurons , we find that when mice are in different positions , different neurons will produce their own electrical signals , as we see in these rectangles .
這些訊號為大腦中的其它區域勾勒出一張地圖 , 持續地向大腦指示出 , " 我現在位於環境中的哪個具體點上 ? "	these signals sketch a map of the rest of the brain constantly indicating to the brain , " where am i in the environment ? "
我們也記錄人腦中的 " 定位神經元細胞 " 。	we also document the location of neurons in the human brain .
癲癇病患者有時需要監測他們的腦電活動情況 。	people with epilepsy sometimes need to monitor their brain activity .
一些患者玩一種電子遊戲 , 遊戲中他們在一個小鎮上自由開車 。	some people played a video game , and they drove freely in a small town .
然後當他們驅車駛過鎮上的某一處時 , 他們大腦海馬區中的 " 定位神經元細胞 " 便會被啟用 , 發出訊號 。	and when they drive drive over town , their cells in the hippocampus are called " locational neurons , " they send out signals .
那麼這 " 定位細胞 " 是怎麼知道老鼠或人處於某個位置的呢 ?	so how does a given cell know that a mouse or a human is in a certain location ?
這裡有兩個神經元細胞 , 它們告訴我們 , 在定位時環境的邊界是至關重要的 。	here are two neurons , and they tell us that the boundary of the positioning environment is essential .
上面的這個細胞傾向於在老鼠向盒子中部走去時產生訊號 。	this cell on the top tends to be signaling as it travels in the middle of the box .
因此當你將盒子擴大 , 相應的訊號活躍區也隨之擴大 。	so when you expand the box , the signal activation zone expands .
下面的這個喜歡在老鼠緊鄰南面屏障時作出反應 。	this one that likes to respond in a tightly neighboring southgrowth barrier .
因此當你在盒中放入另一屏障時 , 不論老鼠在盒中何處 , 只要它的南面有屏障 , 該細胞中的相應位置便會同時產生訊號 。	so when you put another barrier in the box , wherever the mouse is in the box , there's a barrier in the south , and that responds to a signal simultaneously .
這表明瞭解到達邊界比如周邊的建築物等需要的距離和方向對於海馬區的 " 工作 " 而言至關重要 。	it shows that the distance and direction of work that's required to reach the boundaries , such as the buildings around it is critical to the hippocampus .
而且確實 , 在老鼠蒐羅環境時 , 我們在海馬區的輸入訊號中 , 檢測到能對距環境邊界的特定距離與方向作出精確感應的神經元細胞 。	and indeed , in mice arranging , we have input signals in the hippocampus that detect specific distances and directions at the environmental boundaries .

而右面的細胞則是在老鼠南面出現邊界時響應 , 不論這邊界是桌布的垂簾還是一堵牆甚至是兩個被隔開的桌子之間的間隙 。	and the right side of the cell responds in a visiting southern mice , regardless of whether the boundary is a tablecloth curtain or a wall or even a gap between two segregated tables .
以上是我們所推測的一種 " 定位細胞 " 給動物定位的方式 。	so that's one way that we've inferred that positioning cells give the animals their position .
我們也可檢測 , 人類在簡單環境中 , 是怎樣給諸如這面旗這樣的物體定位的或者乾脆把這物體想成你的車 。	we can also test how humans , in a simple environment , give objects such as this flag , or maybe just think of this object as your car .
我們先讓人們熟悉一下環境 , 同時記下物體所在的位置 。	let's get people to be familiar with the environment and note where the object is .
接著 , 再讓他們回到那個環境 , 通常他們都能根據記憶準確無誤地標出物體所在的位置 。	and then , bringing them back to that environment , usually they were able to pinpoint where the object was based on memory precisely mistakes .
但在一些試驗中 , 我們會改變環境的形狀和尺度 , 正如我們在 " 定位細胞 " 實驗中所做的那樣 。	but in some trials , we change the shape and size of the environment just as we do in a targeted cell experiment .
如此 , 我們可以透過研究實驗者改變環境的形狀和尺度 , 來了解旗幟發生了怎樣的位移	so we can change the shape and scale of the environment by studying the experimenter to understand where the flag is moving .
比如現在你所看到的 , 假設這面旗幟在如圖中小四方形內的 " × " 的位置 , 然後接著你問人們小旗在哪 , 但實際上你已經將總環境的尺度擴大了 , 結果他們所認為的旗所在的位置也相應地向外擴張 , 而這擴張的模式和 " 定位細胞 " 的一模一樣 。	so let's say what you're seeing here , suppose that this flag looks like x in the little square of the flag , and then you ask people where the flag is , but actually you've widened the opposite scale of what they think is the flag straight outward towards the outward sprawling , and this pattern of expansion is identical to the position cell .
這就好像你是透過儲存被某一特定位置所激發的 " 定位細胞 " 產生的訊號模式來記憶小旗的位置的 , 接著當你回到那個地點的時候 , 透過四處打量 , 便可以將你當前腦中 " 定位細胞 " 的訊號模式與之前的模式進行匹配 。	it's like the signal pattern that you generate by storing a particular position cell to memorize the flag , and then when you go back to that location , by taking a beat of your brain , you match the signal patterns of a given cell .
這個過程便可讓你回到 " 老地方 " 。	and that allows you to go back to the old place .
我們也能透過位移來給自己定位 。	we can also locate ourselves by giving ourselves a place .
因此當我們外出時或許是我們停車後下來隨便走走我們可以給自己定位 , 因為我們可以粗略地將自己的運動路線與大體的返回方向進行整合 。	so when we're out , maybe we can stop and walk and we can give ourselves a position , because we can roughly integrate our motion circuitry with our bodies backwards .
" 定位細胞 " 也能從一種叫做 " 網狀細胞 " 的細胞那兒獲得此類線路整合的資訊 。	" location cells " also receives information from a cell called a net cell .
目前在向海馬區的訊號輸入中又發現了 " 網狀細胞 " , 它們與 " 定位細胞 " 有點類似 。	right now , inputting the hippocampus signals into the hippocampus , it's a little bit like " location cell . "
隨著老鼠的 " 四處探索 " , 每一個神經元細胞被大量各種位置所激發的訊號組合在一起 , 貫穿整個環境構成一個令人驚歎的規整的三角網格 。	as mice explore , each neuron is combined with signals inspired by locations of locations , through the environment , forming an extraordinary regular grid .
倘若你對一系列 " 網狀細胞 " 進行記錄這裡以不同的顏色區分每一個細胞發出的訊號都能形成網狀 , 遍及整個環境 , 而且每一個細胞的網狀訊號集的位置都與其他細胞有一定偏差 。	if you document a series of net cells , there's a different color distinction , and each cell sends a mesh , colliding through the environment , and every single cell's mesh signal collection has a certain location .
因此紅色標註的細胞訊號集合在這個網格上 , 綠色的是這個 , 而藍色的是這個 。	so the reddigit signals gather on this grid , and the green one is this one , and the blue one is this one .
因此綜合來看 , 這就好像老鼠可以在它所到達的環境中建立一個虛擬的位置訊號網這就有點像你在地圖上所看到的經線和緯線 , 只不過要將線替換成 " 三角形 " 。	so in a synthesis , it's like a mouse can create a virtual location network in its environment and it's kind of like the lines and lines you see on the map , except for the triangle .
當老鼠移動的時候 , 這些電訊號能透過這些細胞傳遞給下一個神經元細胞從而為老鼠定位 , 這樣老鼠就能在運動時知道自己身在何處 。	as the mouse moves , these electrical signals travel through these cells to give the next neuron to its next neuron so that the mice knows where they are in the motion .
那麼人類是否有 " 網狀細胞 " 呢 ?	so does a human have net cells ?
因為所有的網狀訊號集合體都有相同的對稱軸 , 以及相同的網格朝向 , 這裡以橘紅色標識 , 這就意味著大腦中特定部位的所有網狀細胞的聯網行為的變化應該取決於我們是在向著這六個方向運動還是沿著六個方向之間所夾的某一個方向運動 。	because all of the gridlike collections have the same axis and the same grid direction , this is orange labeled here , so what that means is that the network changes in the brain of a specific part of the brain depending on whether we're moving along these six directions or whether we're moving in one direction of the six directions along these six directions .
